<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pas-reaction-for-mucin">PAS Reaction for Mucin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pas-reaction-for-mucin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Remove glycogen from the section by diastase digestion. The staining method is same as for glycogen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="southgate-s-mucicarmine-method">Southgate's mucicarmine method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#southgate-s-mucicarmine-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>While PAS reaction is a histochemical technique, the Southgate's mucicarmine method is an old classical empirical technique which is still very useful in the demonstration of epithelial mucins.</p>
<p><strong>Fixation</strong> Formal saline or most other fixatives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sections">Sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Paraffin section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="preparation-of-mucicarmine">Preparation of mucicarmine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-mucicarmine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Into a 500 ml flask, place 1 g of powdered carmine and 1 g of dry aluminium hydroxide.</li>
<li>Add 100 ml of 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Add 0.5 g of anhydrous aluminium chloride. Shake.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>486 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Boil for 2 <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{1}{2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> minutes.</li>
<li>Cool and filter.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining-procedure">Staining procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Stain nuclei with haematoxylin; differentiate in acid alcohol and blue in tap water (refer to Chapter 7).</li>
<li>Stain for 35–45 minutes in the carmine solution.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in alcohol, clear in xylene and mount in a synthetic medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Epithelial mucin</th><th>red</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Nuclei</td><td>blue</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>
&gt; The quality of carmine cannot be guaranteed and so it is not always possible to prepare a strong staining solution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="99ea5c99">♦ METHODS FOR ACID POLYSACCHARIDES AND MUCOPROTEINS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#99ea5c99" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acid polysaccharides belong to a large group of mucosubstances that are usually not PAS positive. Acid polysaccharides and acid mucoprotein are well demonstrated by alcian blue, Hale’s colloidal iron and metachromatic stains. Sulphated muco-proteins are also PAS negative but can be demonstrated with aldehyde-fuchsin. Other methods that can be used to stain acid mucosubstances include acridine orange (flourochrome dye) and various combinations of the above mentioned staining methods.</p>
<p>Alcian blue with varying electrolyte (MgCl₂) concentrations, selectively stains and distinguishes between strongly and weakly sulphated mucosubstances.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="alcian-blue-methods">Alcian Blue Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcian-blue-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Alcian blue methods are based on the principle that Alcian blue, a copper phthalocyanin basic dye at a low pH will stain acid mucosubstances by salt linkage with acid groups in the tissue.</p>
<p>The pH of the staining solution is 2.5 but when controlled and used at pH 1.0, it will distinguish between acid and sulphated mucoproteins. Alcian blue methods are combined with other techniques to demonstrate and distinguish various mucosubstances in tissue. Neutral mucosubstances may only stain with the PAS reaction. The method for acid polysaccharide is described here.</p>
<p><strong>Fixation</strong> Formal saline
<strong>Sections</strong> Mainly paraffin sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="preparation-of-the-staining-solution">Preparation of the staining solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-the-staining-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Alcian blue</th><th>0.5 g</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Glacial acetic acid</td><td>3 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Distilled water</td><td>100 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Adjust pH to 2.5</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Take section to water.</li>
<li>Stain in alcian blue for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Wash in running water for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Counterstain.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in a synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Acid mucopolysaccharides</th><th>blue</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Nuclei</td><td>red</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9ce117cb">♦ METACHROMATIC STAINING METHODS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9ce117cb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Metachromatic dyes can be used to demonstrate acid mucosubstances. The methods will stain epithelial and connective tissue mucins. The metachromatic methods are quick and simple but they usually do not allow for permanent preparations. Another drawback is that metachaomasia may be variable.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="toluidine-blue-method">Toluidine Blue Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toluidine-blue-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Fixation</strong> Formal saline and other fixatives.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section">Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Paraffin or frozen sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-toluidine-blue">Preparation of toluidine blue<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-toluidine-blue" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dissolve 0.25 g toluidine blue in 100 ml of *Michael’s veronal acetate-hydrochloric acid buffer; pH 4.5</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take sections to water.</li>
<li>Stain in toluidine blue solution for ten seconds.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Examine in watery mount or mount in glycerine jelly. For permanent preparation</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>(i) blot with hard filter paper</li>
<li>(ii) allow to dry</li>
<li>(iii) clear in xylene</li>
<li>(iv) mount in synthetic resin medium</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Metachromatic substances red pink or purple
Nuclei and other constituents blue</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3ea20920">*Michael’s buffer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3ea20920" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>N/10 HCl: 8.5 ml of concentrated HCl per litre.
Titrate against N/10 NaOH.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="veronal-acetate-solution">Veronal acetate solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#veronal-acetate-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sodium acetate crystals
(CH₃COONa·3H₂O) 19.4 g
Sodium diethyl barbiturate (Veronal) 29.4 g
Dissolve in water and make up to 1 litre
Micheal’s buffer pH 4.5: Add 5 ml veronal acetate solution to 11 ml of N/10 HCl</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="da755c39">Schmorl’s Thionin Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#da755c39" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fixation-and-sections">Fixation and sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixation-and-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Same as toluidine blue method</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="stock-solution">Stock solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stock-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Prepare a hot aqueous saturated solution of thionin. Allow to cool.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="working-solution">Working solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#working-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Add 2 drops of stock solution to 5 ml of distilled water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take sections to water</li>
<li>Treat with saturated aqueous mercuric chloride for 30 seconds.</li>
<li>Wash briefly in water.</li>
<li>Stain in the diluted thionin solution for 15–25 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in distilled water.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Metachromatic substances red
Nuclei blue</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uranyl-nitrate-method">Uranyl Nitrate Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uranyl-nitrate-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fixation">Fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Formal saline or other fixatives</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sections">Sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Paraffin sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take sections to water</li>
<li>Oxidise with 1% aqueous potassium permanganate for five minutes</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water</li>
<li>Treat with 5% aqueous oxalic acid until colourless.</li>
<li>Wash well in running tap water.</li>
<li>Stain in 1% toluidine blue for two minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in water.</li>
<li>Rinse in 0.2% aqueous uranyl nitrate until sufficient dye is extracted to give a good colour contrast (usually in about 10–15 seconds).</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water.</li>
<li>Blot.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in absolute alcohol, clear in xylene and mount in synthetic resin medium</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acid mucopolysaccharides red or purple
Acid mucoproteins red or purple
Other tissue constituents blue</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251218-e30d0bca.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="collagen-and-reticulin">COLLAGEN AND RETICULIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#collagen-and-reticulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Collagen consists of coarse extracellular framework (or scaffolding). The collagen fibres are the coarse connective tissue fibres. The fibres stain red with van Gieson's stain; and yellow or brown with silver impregnation. Reticulin comprises a fibrillary extracellular scaffolding found throughout the tissues of the body. The fibrils are delicate and stain black on impregnation with silver and appear as unstained or a faint pink colour with van Gieson's stain. Collagen and reticulin are so similar that some workers believe that they are same, and that reticulin precedes the collagen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="silver-impregnation-methods">Silver impregnation Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#silver-impregnation-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are many methods of silver impregnation of reticulin. They are based on the local reduction and selective precipitation of silver by the aldehyde groups of the carbohydrates of reticulin. Some of these methods depend on silver oxide or hydroxide in ammoniacal solution. Many of these are prepared by producing a precipitate from silver nitrate with sodium, potassium, or ammonium hydroxide or with lithium or sodium carbonate.</p>
<p>Silver impregnation methods require very scrupulous techniques in order to produce reliable consistent results. All glasswares used for the stain and in the staining technique should be thoroughly washed in 10% nitric acid and then rinsed in several changes of distilled water. Plastic forceps should be used for manipulating slides during staining. This is to prevent the non-specific precipitation of silver on the slide if metallic forceps are used. In order to prevent deterioration and precipitation of silver, dust must be avoided. Splashing or the use of glass rods without careful washing between solutions should also be avoided.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="silver-impregnation-for-reticulin-fibres-modified-gomori-s-method">Silver Impregnation for Reticulin Fibres (Modified Gomori's Method)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#silver-impregnation-for-reticulin-fibres-modified-gomori-s-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the most reliable method for demonstrating reticulin fibres and for the differentiation of reticulin and collagen fibres.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-silver-solution">Preparation of Silver Solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-silver-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Add 5 ml of 10% potassium hydroxide to 20 ml of 10% silver nitrate. A precipitate is formed. Mark the fluid level on the flask.</li>
<li>Pour off the supernatant.</li>
<li>Wash the precipitated silver with distilled water twice until the water is clear.</li>
<li>Fill up to the marked level with fresh distilled water. (This gives a clearer solution.)</li>
<li>Add 28% ammonia water drop by drop while continuously shaking until all the precipitate is dissolved.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Staining of Collagen, Reticulum and Elastic Tissue Fibres 459</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Carefully add 10% silver nitrate solution, drop by drop until the precipitate that form disappears on shaking.</li>
<li>Add an equal volume of distilled water to the solution.</li>
<li>Store in a well stoppered dark bottle. It may be used for 2 days.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring paraffin section to water.</li>
<li>Oxidise with 0.5 % aqueous potassium permanganate for two minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled or tap water for two minutes.</li>
<li>Place in two per cent aqueous potassium metabisulphite until colourless (about one minute).</li>
<li>Wash in distilled or tap water for 2–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Place in two per cent aqueous ferric ammonium sulphate for one minute to sensitise.</li>
<li>Wash in distilled or tap water for 1–2 minutes and then for 30 seconds in each of two changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Place in the ammoniacal silver solution to impregnate for one minute.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water for 20 seconds.</li>
<li>Reduce in 20% formalin (10 ml formaldehyde plus 40 ml distilled water) for three minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in distilled water for three minutes.</li>
<li>Tone in 0.2 % gold chloride solution for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water for two minutes.</li>
<li>Place in 3% aqueous potassium metabisulphite for one minute to reduce toning. Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Fix in 2.5 % aqueous sodium thiosulphate (hypo) for 1–2 minute.</li>
<li>Stain with Cole’s haematoxylin for five minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running tap water for five minutes.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Reticulin fibres</th><th>black</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Collagen fibres</td><td>brownish yellow</td></tr><tr><td>Nuclei</td><td>blue</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>The original Gomoris method does not incorporate the staining of nuclei with Cole’s haematoxylin.</li>
<li>Gordon and Sweet’s method makes use of 0.5% aqueous safranin O solution to stain the nuclei.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining-of-collagen">STAINING OF COLLAGEN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-of-collagen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Certain acid aniline dyes such as aniline blue, acid fuchsin, methyl blue and indigo carmine are very useful for the demonstration of collagen and reticulin fibres. They stain selectively with the acid aniline dyes in fairly strong acid solutions. Picric acid is widely employed because in addition to providing acidity and acting as a counterstain for muscle and cell cytoplasm, it forms with the dyes a complex which seems to have a great affinity for collagen. The basis of stains such as van Gieson (Picrofuchsin) is formed on the foregoing reactions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="28ed2cca">Weigert’s Iron-Haematoxylin and van Gieson Stain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#28ed2cca" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a widely used stain for differentiating muscle fibres and connective tissue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="7a5707ee">van Gieson’s Stain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7a5707ee" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Saturated aqueous picric acid</th><th>100 ml</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1% acid fuchsin</td><td>10 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This can be stored as a stock solution, but where possible, a freshly prepared solution of 10 ml saturated aqueous picric acid and 1.5 ml of 1% acid fuchsin may give a better result.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6677c14f">Weigert’s Iron haematoxylin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6677c14f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-haematoxylin-solution-a">1. Haematoxylin (solution A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-haematoxylin-solution-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Haematoxylin</th><th>1 g</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Ethyl alcohol 95%</td><td>100 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>460 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Iron chloride (solution B)
Iron chloride (ferric) 29 %
aqueous solution 4 ml
Hydrochloric acid 1 ml
Distilled water 95 ml</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Working solution
Haematoxylin (solution A) 1 vol
Iron chloride (solution B) 1 vol
Mix well and use within two days</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acid alcohol 1 %</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Procedure</p>
<ol>
<li>Bring sections to water.</li>
<li>Stain with Weigert’s iron haematoxylin for 20 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in tap water.</li>
<li>Differentiate in 1% acid alcohol, blue in tap water (control the degree of differentiation microscopically until the nuclei are just overstained).</li>
<li>Counterstain with van Gieson’s stain for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse rapidly in distilled water or blot lightly. Do not use tap water at this stage.</li>
<li>Dehydrate rapidly in 95% alcohol and ethanol, clear and mount in acid balsam or DPX.</li>
</ol>
<p>Result</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Cell nuclei</th><th>black</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Collagen</td><td>red</td></tr><tr><td>Muscle fibres</td><td>yellow</td></tr><tr><td>Cell cytoplasm</td><td>yellow</td></tr><tr><td>Red blood cells, fibrin</td><td>yellow</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Martin’s Scarlet Blue (MSB) Method for the Demonstration of Collagen Fibres and Fibrin</p>
<p>This stain is used to demonstrate fibrin in contrasting colour to red blood cells.</p>
<p>Reagent solutions
Solution 1 Celestine Blue: Grind 1.0 g celestine blue to a smooth paste in 1.0 ml sulphuric acid. Add 100 ml of 2.5 % aqueous ammonium ferric sulphate. Add 10 ml glycerol and mix thoroughly. Add 0.5 ml sulphuric acid. Filter before use. The solution keeps indefinitely.</p>
<p>Solution 2 10% aqueous chromium trioxide.
Solution 3 Cole’s haematoxylin.
Solution 4 Yellow stain: Dissolve 0.5 g Martin’s yellow and 2.0 g phosphotungstic acid in 100 ml of 95% ethanol.
Solution 5 Red stain: 1.0 g of brilliant cresyl scarlet 6 R in 100 ml of 2.5 % aqueous acetic acid.
Solution 6 1% aqueous phosphotungstic acid.
Solution 7 Blue Stain: 0.5 g of methyl blue in 1 % aqueous acetic acid.</p>
<p>Method</p>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Treat with solution 1 for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running tap water for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Stain with solution 2 for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse with distilled or tap water.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 3 for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running tap water for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in absolute ethanol.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 4 for 2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 5 for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water.</li>
<li>Treat with solution 6 for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 7 for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<p>Results</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Cell nuclei</th><th>blue</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Fibrin</td><td>red</td></tr><tr><td>Collagen</td><td>blue</td></tr><tr><td>Red blood cells</td><td>yellow</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Rapid one Step Trichrome Stain for Connective Tissue (Gomori 1950)</p>
<p>This is a simple trichrome stain that demonstrates collagen fibres well.</p>
<p>Reagent Solutions
Solution 1 Cole’s, Harris or Mayer’s haematoxylin.
Solution 2 Chromotrope 2 R</p>
<p>0.6 g</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Staining of Collagen, Reticulum and Elastic Tissue Fibres 461</p>
<p>Fast green FCF 0.3 g
Phosphotungstic acid 0.6 g
Glacial acetic acid 1.0 ml
Distilled water 100.0 ml
This stain keeps well.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Stain with solution 1 for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash well in tap water.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 2 for 15–20 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse well in 0.2 % acetic acid.</li>
<li>Blot, dehydrate in absolute alcohol, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Collagen</th><th>green</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Cell cytoplasm,</td><td>red</td></tr><tr><td>Muscle, fibrin</td><td>red</td></tr><tr><td>Red blood cells</td><td>red</td></tr><tr><td>Cell nuclei</td><td>blue-black</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3d613c7a">♦ ELASTIC FIBRES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3d613c7a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Elastic tissue is present in many animal tissues such as skin, ligaments, blood vessels, lung and especially in the wall of aorta. It occurs as fine, sometimes branching fibres like in the dermis, or in laminated sheets as in blood vessels. It is subject to alteration, e.g., the wrinkled skin of old age is largely due to atrophy of elastic fibres.</p>
<p>Elastic fibres are very insoluble in organic and inorganic solvents, unlike the collagen fibres that are swollen and soluble in 2% acetic acid. They are resistant to most enzymes except elastase of the pancreas, and also resistant to autolytic changes. Elastic tissue is autofluorescent and gives greenish yellow (blue if unstained) fluorescence in ultra violet light. Elastic fibres are stained by both acid and basic dyes. Many methods are available for their selective staining but most of the staining methods are empirical. For most of the staining methods, fixation is not critical.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1846013e">Gomori’s Aldehyde-Fuchsin Method for Elastic Fibres<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1846013e" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="reagent-solutions">Reagent Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagent-solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="solution-1-aldehyde-fuchsin">Solution 1 (Aldehyde-fuchsin)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-1-aldehyde-fuchsin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Basic fuchsin</th><th>0.5 g</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>70% ethanol</td><td>100.0 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Paraldehyde (USP)</td><td>1.0 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Concentrated HCl</td><td>1.0 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Dissolve the fuchsin in alcohol and add the paraldehyde and hydrochloric acid. Shake well and leave at room temperature for 24–48 hours, until it is deep purple and ready for use. Store in the refrigerator for up to 3 months.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="solution-2">Solution 2<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Lugol’s iodine (refer to Chapter 8)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="solution-3-light-green">Solution 3 (Light green)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-3-light-green" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Light green SF</th><th>0.2 g</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Orange G</td><td>1.0 g</td></tr><tr><td>Chromotrope 2R (optional)</td><td>0.5 g</td></tr><tr><td>Phosphotungstic acid</td><td>0.5 g</td></tr><tr><td>Glacial acetic acid</td><td>1.0 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Distilled water</td><td>100.0 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Treat with Lugol’s iodine for 30 minutes.</li>
<li>Bleach in 5% sodium thiosulphate for two minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running tap water for 3 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in 90% ethanol.</li>
<li>Stain in aldehyde-fuchsin for 5–10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in 90% ethanol.</li>
<li>Counterstain with light green.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Elastic fibres</th><th>:deep purple</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Collagen</td><td><span style="color: rgb(21, 130, 55);"></span></td></tr><tr><td>Granules of mast cells</td><td>:deep purple</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="10e48322">Verhoeff’s Elastic Fibre Stain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10e48322" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Verhoeff’s solution To 30 ml of 5% alcoholic haematoxylin, add 12 ml of 10% aqueous ferric</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<p>chloride (FeCl₃); mix and then add 12 ml of Lugol's iodine and mix.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>De-wax and hydrate paraffin section.</li>
<li>Stain in Verhoeff's solution until the section is black (about 20–45 minutes).</li>
<li>Differentiate in 2% aqueous FeCl₃, controlling the degree of differentiation microscopically - (until only elastic fibres and cell nuclei are black and other tissues are grey). If the section is over differentiated, it may be returned to Verhoeff's solution for further staining.</li>
<li>Rinse in water and then transfer to 95% alcohol to remove iodine.</li>
<li>Wash in water for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Counterstain with van Gieson stain (refer to staining of collagen) for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Elastic fibres</th><th>:black</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Nuclei</td><td><span style="color: rgb(0, 104, 201);"></span> to black</td></tr><tr><td>Collagen</td><td><span style="color: rgb(255, 43, 43);"></span></td></tr><tr><td>Muscle fibres,</td><td>:yellow</td></tr><tr><td>Red blood cells</td><td>:yellow</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="orcein-and-methylene-blue-method-modified-taenzer-unna-orcein-method">Orcein and Methylene Blue Method (Modified Taenzer-Unna Orcein Method)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orcein-and-methylene-blue-method-modified-taenzer-unna-orcein-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method demonstrates fine and delicate elastic fibres</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reagent-solutions">Reagent solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagent-solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Solution 1</strong> Dissolve 1.0 g synthetic orcein in 100 ml of 70% alcohol. Add 1.0 ml hydrochloric acid. This solution keeps indefinitely.
<strong>Solution 2</strong> 0.5% methylene blue in 1.0% acetic acid.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Bring sections to 70% alcohol.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stain in solution 1 in a covered jar for 30 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse off excess stain with 70% alcohol.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stain in solution 2 for 2–3 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse off excess stain with distilled water and blot gently with filter paper.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Elastic fibres</th><th>:light to deep brown</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Nuclei</td><td><span style="color: rgb(0, 104, 201);"></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="resorcin-fuchsin-stain">Resorcin-Fuchsin Stain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resorcin-fuchsin-stain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a very useful staining method for the denonstration of elastic fibres. A better result is obtained when the method is used in conjunction with connective tissue stains such as the van Gieson stain. It is very good for photography.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reagent-solutions">Reagent solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagent-solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Solution 1</strong> Just before use, mix equal parts of 0.3% potassium permanganate and 0.3% sulphuric acid.
<strong>Solution 2</strong> 5% oxalic acid in distilled water.
<strong>Solution 3</strong> To boiling 200 ml distilled water slowly add:</p>
<ul>
<li>1.0 g crystal violet</li>
<li>1.0 g basic fuchsin</li>
<li>4.0 g resorcin</li>
<li>0.5 g dextrin</li>
</ul>
<p>Allow the ingredients to dissolve. Slowly add 25 ml of 10% ferric chloride solution. Boil for further 5 minutes. Allow to cool, and then filter. Add the precipitate on the filter paper to 100 ml of 95% alcohol, and leave it overnight.</p>
<p>Simmer gently for 1 hour and then cool. Add 100 ml of 95% alcohol and 6 ml hydrochloric acid. This is the stock solution and it can keep in definitely.</p>
<p><strong>Solution 4</strong> Working elastic fibre stain solution
<strong>Solution 3</strong> 3 parts
<strong>1% hydrochloric acid in 70% alcohol</strong> 7 parts</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Treat with solution 1 for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse with distilled water.</li>
<li>Treat with solution 2 for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash well with distilled water.</li>
<li>Leave in 70% alcohol for 1 minute.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Staining of Collagen, Reticulum and Elastic Tissue Fibres 463</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>
<p>Place in solution 4 for from 6 to 18 hours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash off excess stain with 70% alcohol.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in running tap water for 2 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counterstain with any appropriate red nuclear stain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dehydrate, clear and mount in a synthetic medium.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Elastic fibres: dark blue to jet black
Background according to counterstain.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251218-5812f52d.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<p>Pigments are substances found in living matter. They absorb visible light. They differ in their origin, composition and significance. Pigments are classified into (i) Artifacts (ii) Endogenous pigments, and (iii) Exogenous pigments.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="artifacts">ARTIFACTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#artifacts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are pigments that result from methods used during processing of the tissues.</p>
<p><strong>Formalin pigment</strong> This is a dark brown pigment formed by the action of acidic formaldehyde on blood. The pigment is also known as acid formaldehyde haematein. It is removed by treating sections with alcoholic picric acid.</p>
<p><strong>Mercuric pigments</strong> These are grey black granular deposits resulting from the use of mercury containing fixatives. They are removed by treating sections with alcoholic iodine, followed by sodium thiosulphate.</p>
<p><strong>Chrome deposits</strong> These brownish black granular deposits result when tissues fixed in chrome fixatives are treated with alcohol. The chrome-fixed tissues must be washed in running tap water for 12 to 18 hours in order to remove excess chromate from the tissue before dehydration in alcohol.</p>
<p><strong>Stain precipitates</strong> These are highly coloured, amorphous and granular precipitates seen in stained sections. They result from improper staining procedures. They are common if saturated solution of stain is allowed to evaporate or dry up on the section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endogenous-pigments">ENDOGENOUS PIGMENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endogenous-pigments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="haemoglobin">HAEMOGLOBIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemoglobin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Haemoglobin is the most widely encountered haematogenous pigment in the tissue. Despite its presence in large amounts in all tissues, it is difficult to stain. It is poorly preserved following fixation in such fixatives as 'Susa'; it is well stained by acid dyes after fixation in formalin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dunn-thompson-method-for-haemoglobin">Dunn Thompson Method for Haemoglobin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dunn-thompson-method-for-haemoglobin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This staining method gives very reliable and quick results. It is a modified van Gieson staining method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Stain in matured aqueous solution of alum haematoxylin for 15 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in tap water.</li>
<li>Mordant for 1 minute in aqueous solution of 4% ferric ammonium sulphate (iron alum).</li>
<li>Stain in the aqueous alum haematoxylin solution for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse rapidly in tap water.</li>
<li>Stain in van Gieson solution.</li>
<li>Transfer directly to 95% alcohol and differentiate for 1–3 minutes.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Demonstration of Pigments 465</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong>
Red blood corpuscles : greenish-black
Haemoglobin casts or ingested haemoglobin : light shades of green</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong>
Staining in haematoxylin two times gives a sharper colour reaction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="benzidine-method-for-haemoglobin">Benzidine Method for Haemoglobin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benzidine-method-for-haemoglobin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This staining reaction is based on the action of the enzyme peroxidase in the transfer of oxygen from hydrogen peroxide, oxidising benzidine to a blue dye. It can be applied to both frozen and paraffin sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reagent-solutions">Reagent solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagent-solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Solution 1</strong> Dissolve 0.5 g benzidine in 50 ml of absolute alcohol
Dissolve 0.1 g of sodium nitroprusside in 10 ml of distilled water.
Mix and make up to 100 ml with distilled water.</p>
<p><strong>Solution 2</strong></p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Absolute alcohol</th><th>50.0 ml</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Glacial acetic acid</td><td>2.0 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Hydrogen peroxide (30%)</td><td>0.5 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Sodium nitroprusside</td><td>0.1 g</td></tr><tr><td>Distilled water</td><td>100.0 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Wash in distilled water for 30 minutes.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 1 for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Stain in solution 2 for 20–30 minutes. Control microscopically. Erythrocytes should become black with a light grey background.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in 70% alcohol and in a mixture of 90% alcohol and 2% acetic acid.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in absolute alcohol, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Erythrocytes black
Other tissues light grey</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Both solutions 1 and 2 must be prepared fresh.</li>
<li>The stained sections should be stored in the dark as sunlight bleaches the stain.</li>
<li>Benzidine is carcinogenic; substitutes such as 3-amino-9 ethylcarbazole may be used.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="haemosiderins">HAEMOSIDERINS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemosiderins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Haemoglobin, when released from the red cells, is broken down into iron-free haematoidin and iron containing haemosiderin. The haemosiderin consists of ferric hydroxide (Fe(OH)₃) bound to protein, ferritin. Haemosiderin appears in about 2 or 3 days after the release of haemoglobin, though small amount of haemosiderin is normally present in the spleen and bone marrow. It becomes abundant in tissues in conditions such as pernicious anaemia, haemosiderosis and haemochromatosis. It is a granular, yellowish brown pigment; soluble in acids but not in alkalis. For this reason, buffered neutral formalin should be used for fixation.</p>
<p>There are several methods for the demonstration of haemosiderin in tissue. The most popular and perhaps the best method is the Perls’ Prussian blue reaction. It is important to use iron free reagents and equipments in order to prevent the contamination of the section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="22a819aa">Perls’ Prussian blue reaction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#22a819aa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The principle of this reaction is based on the combination of ferric (inorganic) iron with potassium ferrocyanide in acid solution to form ferric ferrocyanide (Prussian blue):</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mn>4</mn><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow><mn>3</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mn>3</mn><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mn>4</mn></msub><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>6</mn></msub><mo>⟶</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">4\mathrm{FeCl}_3 + 3\mathrm{K}_4\mathrm{Fe(CN)}_6 \longrightarrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8444em; <p>[Ferric chloride] [Ferric iron potassium ferrocyanide]</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mn>4</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>6</mn></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mn>3</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mn>12</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{Fe}_4[\mathrm{Fe(CN)}_6]_3 + 12\mathrm{KCl}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.0497em; vertical-align: -0.2997em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Fe</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">4</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Fe</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathrm">CN</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.4003em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">6</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2997em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em;
