margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord">12</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">KCl</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>[Ferric ferrocyanide] [Potassium Chloride]</p>
<p>The ferric ferrocyanide is an insoluble precipitate. This reaction is a specific histochemical reaction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to tap water.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>466 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Stain with a mixture of equal volumes of 2% potassium ferrocyanide and 2% hydrochloric acid in distilled water for 20-30 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counterstain with 0.5% aqueous eosin for 20-50 seconds; or 1% aqueous neutral red for 20-60 seconds, or 0.1% safranin for 10-30 seconds, or van Gieson for 1-3 minutes or 0.1% nuclear fast red in 5% aluminium sulphate for 2-5 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Haemosiderin and ferric salts : blue
Cell nuclei : pink to red</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<p>Gomori’s modification (1952) of this procedure tends to give the sharpest staining. Place section in freshly made 10% aqueous potassium ferrocyanide (note the volume of ferrocyanide solution) for 5-10 minutes. Then add 10% solution of HCl in an amount equal to half the volume of the ferrocyanide solution used. Mix by stirring with a clean glass rod and leave for 20 minutes. The reason for improved result is because the potassium ferrocyanide diffuses more slowly than hydrochloric acid, so that if mixed with the latter, it’s action may be too late to have good effect on the ferric irons in the correct part of the tissue. By this method, the ferrocyanide is present in the tissue when the ferric salts are released.</p>
<p><strong>INORGANIC IRON</strong></p>
<p>Almost all the iron in tissues is in the ferric state, and the Prussian blue reaction is very adequate in demonstrating it. Ferric iron, however, can be converted to ferrous iron by ammonium sulphide and in the process form the black iron sulphide (Quincker’s reaction). This ferrous sulphide is stained by Turnbull blue reaction.</p>
<p><strong>Turnbull’s Blue Reaction for Ferrous Iron</strong></p>
<p>This staining reaction is based on the formation of a blue precipitate (Turnbull’s blue) by the reaction between ferrous salts and potassium ferrocyanide.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>3</mn><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mn>2</mn><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mn>3</mn></msub><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>6</mn></msub><mo>⟶</mo><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mn>3</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>6</mn></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mn>6</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3\mathrm{FeCl}_2 + 2\mathrm{K}_3\mathrm{Fe(CN)}_6 \longrightarrow \mathrm{Fe}_3[\mathrm{Fe(CN)}_6]_2 + 6\mathrm{KCl}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8444em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">FeCl</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.0497em; vertical-align: -0.2997em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">K</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Fe</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathrm">CN</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.4003em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">6</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2997em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">⟶</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.0497em; vertical-align: -0.2997em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Fe</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Fe</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathrm">CN</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.4003em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">6</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2997em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">KCl</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p><strong>Method</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to tap water.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in a freshly prepared solution of equal parts of 20% potassium ferricyanide and 2% hydrochloric acid in distilled water for 10-15 minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer to 1% hydrochloric acid for 10-15 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Counterstain in van Gieson solution as for Perl’s reaction.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Ferrous Salts : blue
Other pigments : unstained</p>
<p><strong>BILE PIGMENTS</strong></p>
<p>Bile pigments are iron-free and appear days after haemosiderin has appeared. The usual method of staining the bile pigments is by Gmelin’s reaction, although Stein’s iodine method is also used. Pigments are soluble in tissues and they do not give primary fluorescence.</p>
<p><strong>Gmelin’s Method for Bile Pigments</strong></p>
<p>This staining method is based on the progressive oxidation of bilirubin into various coloured compounds. Negative reactions should be repeated two or three times before being reported as negative.</p>
<p><strong>Method</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to tap water.</li>
<li>Mount a section in water under a coverslip and find the pigment.</li>
<li>Leave the slide on the microscope under high power objective.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Demonstration of Pigments 467</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Apply a drop of strong nitric acid to one side of the coverslip with a pasteur pipette.</li>
<li>Put a small piece of dry filter on the opposite side of the coverslip so as to draw the nitric acid through the section.</li>
<li>Immediately watch the pigment through the microscope for a change of colour.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong> In a few seconds, the yellowish-brown pigment will change to green, then to blue and purple.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2262be1d">Stein’s Iodine Test for Bile Pigments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2262be1d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is based on the oxidation of the pigments to green bilverdin by iodine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Stain in a mixture of three parts of Lugol’s iodine and 1 part of tincture of iodine*.</li>
<li>Leave overnight.</li>
<li>Wash in running tap water for five minutes.</li>
<li>Decolourise with 5% aqueous sodium thiosulphate for 30 seconds.</li>
<li>Rinse in water.</li>
<li>Counterstain with 1% neutral red for five minutes.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in acetone, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<p>*Tincture of iodine is a saturated alcoholic solution of iodine</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Bilirubin : green
Nuclei : red
Other pigments : natural colours</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="69c13760">♦ MELANIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#69c13760" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Melanin is a granular black or yellowish-brown pigment that is normally present in the skin, hair, eye (choroid and iris), meniniges and substantial nigra of the brain. It is formed from tyrosine by the action of tyrosinase (DOPA oxidase which converts the tyrosine into di-hydroxyphenylalanine i.e. DOPA and then into melanin). Melanin is insoluble in organic solvents but soluble in 1M sodium hydroxide. It is slowly bleached by strong oxidising agents such as hydrogen peroxide, potassium permanganate, ferric chloride and ascorbic acid. Solutions of ammoniacal silver nitrate are reduced by melanin to black metallic silver. This is the basis of the Masson-Fontana method of demonstrating melanin.</p>
<p>In pathological conditions such as benign and malignant melanomas, melanin is found in variable amounts, and its demonstration in tissues may be very decisive. Identification of a pigment as melanin may depend on a negative Prussian blue reaction, a positive argentaffin (silver) reaction and positive melanin bleach, while of course bearing in mind the situation of the pigment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="masson-fontana-ammoniacal-silver-reaction-for-melanin">Masson-Fontana Ammoniacal Silver Reaction for Melanin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#masson-fontana-ammoniacal-silver-reaction-for-melanin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is the argentaffin reaction which is based on the ability of tyrosine derivatives to reduce silver solutions to metallic silver.</p>
<p><strong>Silver solution</strong> Add strong (28%) ammonia water drop by drop to 20 ml of 10% aqueous silver nitrate until the dark brown precipitate that forms is almost redissolved (about 2 ml ammonia water will do it).</p>
<p>Add 20 ml distilled water and leave to stand for 18–24 hours. Place the supernatant in a dark brown bottle and it will keep for weeks. Filter before use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Treat with Gram’s iodine solution for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash well in several changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Place the section in the silver solution in the dark for 18–24 hours.</li>
<li>Rinse in three changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Tone in 0.1% gold chloride for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Fix in 5% sodium thiosulphate for two minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in running tap water for two minutes.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>468 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="10">
<li>Counterstain with 0.5% safranin or 1% neutral red for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in water, and rapidly in 70% alcohol.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong>
Melanin : black
Argentaffin cell granules : black</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong> Melanin granules are also argyrophilic (i.e. they are capable of binding silver salts which may be subsequently reduced by a reducing agent to give a black deposit of silver).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bleaching-methods-for-melanin">Bleaching Methods for Melanin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bleaching-methods-for-melanin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>40% paracetic acid method</strong> This solution acts rapidly as a bleaching agent. Melanin is bleached within 2–14 hours. Lipofuscin pigment resists decolourisation for longer than 16 hours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="chlorate-method">Chlorate method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chlorate-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Take section down to 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Add a small quantity of potassium chlorate at the bottom of a coplin jar.</li>
<li>Fill to the mark with 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Place the section in the jar.</li>
<li>Using a pipette, add 3 or 4 drops of concentrated hydrochloric acid to the bottom of the jar.</li>
<li>Leave section for 24 hours.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Peroxide method</strong> Place the section in 30 vol of 10% hydrogen peroxide and leave for 24–36 hours.</p>
<p><strong>Permanganate method</strong> The sections are treated with 0.1% potassium permanganate for 12 hours.</p>
<p>Rinse in water and stain with 1% oxalic acid for 1 minute.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Bleaching methods are not specific for melanin.</li>
<li>Control staining reaction microscopically.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lipofuscin-pigment">LIPOFUSCIN PIGMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lipofuscin-pigment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The lipofuscin pigments are widely distributed in the animal tissues. They are a group of substances of variable structures. They are produced by a steady process of oxidation of lipid. They reduce silver and ferricyanide solutions. They give strong positive reaction with Sudan black while being negative with other fat-soluble stains. The lipofuscins are also PAS positive but are usually demonstrated by their reduction of Schmorl’s ferricyanide.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4c566a24">Schmorl’s Method for Lipofuscin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4c566a24" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The principle of this method is based on the reduction of ferricyanide to ferrocyanide, with the formation of a dark blue iron complex.</p>
<p><strong>Iron ferricyanide</strong> Mix 4 ml fresh 1% potassium ferricyanide solution in distilled water with 30 ml of 1% ferric chloride solution in distilled water. Add 6 ml distilled water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in the iron ferricyanide solution for 10 minutes at room temperature.</li>
<li>Wash rapidly in 1% aqueous acetic acid solution.</li>
<li>Wash in water.</li>
<li>Counterstain with 1% neutral red for 3 minutes.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in a neutral synthetic medium.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong>
Lipofuscins : dark blue
Other reducing substances : blue</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong> Include a control slide for Turnbull blue staining because ferricyanide in the mixture can react with any available ferrous salts. A negative Turnbull blue reaction and a positive Schmorl’s method, is indicative.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Demonstration of Pigments 469</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="miscellaneous-endogenous-pigments">Miscellaneous Endogenous Pigments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#miscellaneous-endogenous-pigments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are other endogenous pigments whose identification by simple histotechniques is not practical. The argentaffin granules of the intestinal glands do reduce silver solutions to metallic silver and are positive with Schmorl’s blue method. These granules are soluble in alcohol and so avoid the use of alcohol containing fixatives. The chromaffin granules of the adrenal medulla are tiny brown pigmented granules following treatment of fresh tissue with chromic acid or chrome salts. For further classification and identification of these pigments, the reader is advised to refer to any standard text book of Histopathology.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="exogenous-pigments">EXOGENOUS PIGMENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exogenous-pigments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Exogenous pigments are those extraneous substances, often coloured, opaque or crystalline, found in tissues. It is often necessary to classify and identify these materials in order not to confuse them with naturally occurring pigments. The identification of these pigments are beyond the scope of this book. The commonest ones among them are:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="carbon">Carbon<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carbon" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most common exogenous pigment in the tissue is carbon. The accumulation of carbon dust and coal dust in the lungs and lymphatic tissue causes anthracosis. Its distribution may be focal or may affect the entire organ. When seen under intense light, it is a yellowish brown particle. It is insoluble in all known solvents, and resists bleaching. It is usually recognised by its site.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iron-ore-pigments">Iron ore Pigments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iron-ore-pigments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The iron ore pigments may be found in the lungs of coal miners. The pigments are variably coloured. They may give positive reaction with Prussian blue and Turnbull’s blue staining methods.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="copper">Copper<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#copper" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Copper is seen in the liver with an increased level in cirrhosis and in Wilson’s disease. It is demonstrated by the rubeanic acid method in which the acid combines with copper salts to produce a coloured complex (copper rubeanate).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="asbestos">Asbestos<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#asbestos" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Asbestos occurs in tissues as long thin crystalline needles or as elongated beaded rods with large rounded ends. They are gold-yellow in colour when unstained and usually give a positive Prussian blue reaction. Asbestos is easily demonstrated in an unstained section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="calcium">Calcium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calcium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Calcium salts are present in bones and teeth, but under abnormal conditions, calcium salt deposits may be found in any part of the tissues such as lymph nodes, hyaline cartilage, fibroids and so on. They can also be found in the foci of infection with <em>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</em> and <em>Histoplasma capsulatum</em>.</p>
<p>Special stains for the demonstration of calcium salts include the Alizarin red S and the von Kossa methods. The latter is described below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9d3181f5">von Kossa’s Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9d3181f5" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is a metal substitution technique, and depends on the replacement of the calcium part of the calcium salts (calcium carbonate or calcium phosphate) and so it is not specific for the calcium itself. Sections are treated with silver nitrate solution and the silver is deposited presumably replacing the calcium, reduced by the action of strong light and thereby seen as metallic silver. It is an old and most widely used method for the demonstration of pathological calcification and calcified bones.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>5% aqueous solution of silver nitrate (it should be colourless).</li>
<li>3% aqueous solution of sodium thiosulphate.</li>
<li>0.2% safranin O in 1% acetic acid.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to distilled water.</li>
<li>Immerse slide in (or flood slide with) solution 1 for 5–10 minutes.</li>
<li>Expose the slide to bright sunlight or ultra violet light for 10–20 minutes or to a 60 watt electric bulb placed about 10 cm away for 60 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash slide in several changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Treat with solution 2 to remove unreacted silver for two minutes.</li>
<li>Counterstain with solution 3 for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse well in several changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Blot gently with filter paper.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic mounting medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Calcium deposits : black to brown-black
Nuclei : red
Cytoplasm : pink</p>
<p>&gt; Note:
&gt; 1. Urates in the tissue may give positive result. Include a control slide treated with aqueous lithium carbonate or 10% aqueous HCl. This slide should give negative result.
&gt; 2. Alcohol containing fixatives give the best results.
&gt; 3. Calcium oxalate is believed to be negative with this method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lipochromes">Lipochromes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lipochromes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are organic exogenous pigments which are of vegetable origin and are found in tissues. They are usually oil-soluble, reddish-yellow in colour and are usually dissolved out by clearing agents during processing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unknown-pigments">Unknown Pigments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unknown-pigments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Histotechnologists often come across unknown pigments in sections. These pigments can be identified using specific and non-specific staining methods. The simple routine staining methods may give a good clue as to the type, depending on the appearance and situation in the tissue, and by exclusion the exact identification of the unknown pigment can be made.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Chapter 11</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staining-of-microorganisms-in-tissues">Staining of Microorganisms in Tissues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-of-microorganisms-in-tissues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining-of-bacteria">STAINING OF BACTERIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-of-bacteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bacteria are microscopic unicellular organisms and they are ubiquitous. A simple classification of bacteria may be based on their morphology—spherical (coccus), rod shaped (bacillus) or spiral (spirillum), or by their staining characteristics. Histological methods are not the best for the identification of bacteria. Bacterial culture is by far superior and more specific. Therefore where possible, a swab from the tissue or unfixed piece of tissue should be sent to the Bacteriology department for culture and identification. It is however still important for the histotechnologist to be able to give a simple general identification of bacteria when seen in the tissue. The most commonly used staining methods in the histopathology laboratory for demonstrating bacteria include the Grams stain or its modifications, acid-fast techniques and certain silver methods.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gram-s-staining-method">Gram's Staining Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gram-s-staining-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This staining method is named after the bacteriologist, Christian Gram (1884). It is the most classical and most informative routine stain for the demonstration of bacteria in tissue sections. It classifies bacteria into two groups: Gram Positive bacteria which retain the primary stain after treatment with alcohol or acetone, and Gram Negative bacteria which are 'decolourised' of the primary colour by alcohol or acetone. It is a regressive staining method. The bacteria are first stained with a strong basic aniline dye, then treated with iodine solution and differentiated (decolourised) with alcohol or acetone for a brief period of time. The Gram positive bacteria retain the stain while the Gram negative bacteria which lose the stain are counterstained with dilute carbol fuchsin, safranin or neutral red.</p>
<p><strong>Principle</strong> There are several theories to explain the Gram's reaction. Basically, the method depends on the differential solubility of the aniline stain in alcohol or acetone when the stain is adsorbed by the bacteria. The iodine which acts as a mordant, forms a dye lake complex that colours both the Gram positive and Gram negative cells blue-black. The decolourising agent (alcohol or acetone) extracts the stain from the Gram negative bacteria more readily than from the Gram positive bacteria. The action of the decolourising agent is relative rather than an absolute one. If the bacteria are exposed to the action of the decolourising agent for too long, the Gram positive bacteria can be decolourised, hence this stage of the staining method should be carefully controlled.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="brown-brenn-modified-gram-s-stain">Brown-Brenn Modified Gram's Stain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#brown-brenn-modified-gram-s-stain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This modification of the Gram's stain is ideal for sections. It gives good colour contrasts.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>472 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3c0619d0">Solution 1 (Hucker’s ammonium oxalate crystal violet)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3c0619d0" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>10% alcoholic solution of crystal violet 2 ml</li>
<li>1% aqueous solution of ammonium oxalate 80 ml</li>
<li>Distilled water 18 ml</li>
<li>Mix and filter before use. Solution is stable for 3–6 months.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3525b6b2">Solution 2 (Grams’s Iodine)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3525b6b2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Potassium iodide (KI) 2 g</li>
<li>Iodine 1 g</li>
<li>Distilled water 300 ml</li>
<li>Dissolve the KI in distilled water, then dissolve the iodine in the KI solution.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solution-3">Solution 3<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-3" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Equal parts mixture of ethyl ether and acetone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solution-4-alcoholic-basic-fuchsin">Solution 4 (Alcoholic basic fuchsin)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-4-alcoholic-basic-fuchsin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>5 ml of 0.1% basic fuchsin in 95% ethanol diluted to 60 ml with distilled water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solution-5-picric-acid-acetone-solution">Solution 5 (Picric acid-acetone solution)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-5-picric-acid-acetone-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Anhydrous picric acid 0.1 g</li>
<li>Acetone 100 ml</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>De-wax and hydrate sections.</li>
<li>Stain with solution 1 for 1 minute.</li>
<li>Rinse in water.</li>
<li>Treat with solution 2 for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in water and blot with filter paper without leaving it completely dry.</li>
<li>Decolourise with solution 3 (or rapidly with acetone) until no more blue colour runs off.</li>
<li>Stain with solution 4 for 1 minute.</li>
<li>Wash in water.</li>
<li>Blot gently but not completely dry.</li>
<li>Dip in acetone for 10–15 seconds.</li>
<li>Treat briefly with picric acid-acetone to decolourise the background tissue until it becomes brownish-yellow (15–30 seconds).</li>
<li>Pass quickly through two changes of acetone-xylene mixture.</li>
<li>Pass through two changes of xylene.</li>
<li>Mount in a synthetic mounting medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Gram positive bacteria : blue-black</li>
<li>Gram negative bacteria : red</li>
<li>Nuclei : red</li>
<li>Other tissue elements : yellow</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>
&gt; 1. Ethyl ether is highly flammable and volatile. Do not use near any naïve flame.
&gt; 2. The picric acid must be anhydrous (dried in vacuum desiccator over calcium chloride).
&gt; 3. The picric acid-acetone mixture must be yellow. If greenish tint is visible, discard it.
&gt; 4. Complete dryness at any stage of the staining will lead to the formation of insoluble compounds that will not be decolourised by ether-acetone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gram-weigert-method-for-bacteria">Gram-Weigert Method for Bacteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gram-weigert-method-for-bacteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this method, counterstaining is performed before the Gram’s stain, and decolourisation is slowly carried out with aniline-xylene.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solution-1-lithium-carmine">Solution 1-Lithium carmine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-1-lithium-carmine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Dissolve 4 g carmine in 100 ml saturated lithium carbonate solution. Boil for 10–15 minutes. When cool, add 1 g thymol as preservative. Filter before use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solution-2">Solution 2<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Hucker’s crystal violet solution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solution-3">Solution 3<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-3" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Gram-Weigert iodine</p>
<p>Potassium Iodide 2 g, dissolved in 50 ml distilled water, Iodine 1 g dissolved in the KI solution and volume made up to 100 ml with distilled water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>De-wax and hydrate sections.</li>
<li>Stain nuclei for 5 minutes in solution 1.</li>
<li>Treat with acid-alcohol for a few seconds.</li>
<li>Wash well in tap water.</li>
<li>Stain with solution 2 for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Blot gently with filter paper.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Staining of Microorganisms in Tissues 473</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Treat with solution 3 for 1/2 minute.</li>
<li>Blot gently with filter paper.</li>
<li>Decolourise with equal parts mixture of aniline xylene. Blot and pour on fresh aniline-xylene several times until no more purple colour washes off. Blot and rinse in 3 or 4 changes of xylene to remove the aniline.</li>
<li>Mount in a synthetic mounting medium.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Gram positive bacteria : blue black
Gram negative bacteria : red
Nuclei : red</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>
&gt; This modification of the Gram's stain also demonstrates fibrin which stains blue-black like the Gram positive bacteria. The acid-alcohol preserves the red colour during subsequent staining.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4aa4a245">Gram’s Stain for Smears<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4aa4a245" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the traditional Gram’s method designed for bacterial smears.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Heat fix air dried smears. Perform staining on the staining rack.</li>
<li>Stain with 1% aqueous or Hucker’s solution of crystal violet for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash with water.</li>
<li>Mordant with Gram’s or Lugol’s iodine for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash with water.</li>
<li>Decolourise with acetone for 1–2 seconds or with 95% ethanol for 30–60 seconds.</li>
<li>Wash well with water.</li>
<li>Counterstain with 0.5% aqueous solution of safranin O, or 0.5% aqueous solution of neutral red or with dilute (1:10) carbol fuchsin for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash with water, blot dry and examine with oil immersion.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Gram positive bacteria : blue-black
Gram negative bacteria : red</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acid-fast-staining">Acid-fast Staining<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acid-fast-staining" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A certain group of bacteria is acid fast i.e. they resist decolourisation with acid when stained with a strong stain. These acid fast bacteria belong to the Genus <em>Mycobacterium</em>, several species of which are pathogenic for man. They include <em>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</em> (causative agent of tuberculosis), <em>Mycobacterium leprae</em> (causative agent of leprosy), and various other species known as atypical mycobacteria. Some members of the group are also alcohol fast, e.g., <em>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</em>. This property of acid and/or acid-alcohol fastness is due to the high lipid content of the bacterial cell wall.</p>
<p>Certain species of <em>Nocardia</em>, a fungus like bacterium, e.g., <em>Nocardia asteroides</em> and <em>Nocardia brasiliensis</em>, are also acid fast.</p>
<p>The tuberculous lesions in the tissues very much look like those of sarcoid or other granulomatous malignant conditions. This makes the identification of tubercle bacilli important for proper diagnosis.</p>
<p>The traditional staining method of acid fast bacilli is the Ziehl Neelsen’s method. The staining procedure is simple enough but microscopic examination of the section is time consuming. A laboratory that handles many samples needs a faster screening method. The fluorescence method for the microscopic identification of mycobacteria is very useful. Such stained sections or smears are examined with the ultra violet light, and the acid fast bacilli fluoresce brilliantly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="79b2d96d">Ziehl Neelsen’s method for acid-fast bacteria in tissue<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#79b2d96d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The method depends on the resistance of tubercle bacilli to acid or acid-alcohol after staining with hot carbol fuchsin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Carbol fuchsin
Basic fuchsin 1 g
Absolute ethyl alcohol 10 ml
Phenol crystals 5 g
Distilled water 100 ml</li>
</ol>
<p>Dissolve the basic fuchsin in the ethyl alcohol and the phenol in water. Mix the two solutions. Filter before use.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>474 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Acid-alcohol
1% hydrochloric acid in 70% alcohol.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counterstain-methylene blue or malachite green
1% aqueous solution of methylene blue or 0.5% aqueous solution of malachite green</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Procedure</p>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to water.</li>
<li>Flood the slide with the carbol fuchsin. Heat from underneath until steam rises. Reheat at three intervals of five minutes each (or stain in a jar at 37°C for 1 hour, or at 56°C for 30 minutes, or overnight at room temperature).</li>
<li>Wash well in tap water.</li>
<li>Decolourise with 1% acid-alcohol until a faint pink colour is retained.</li>
<li>Wash in water.</li>
<li>Counterstain with the 1% methylene blue or 0.5% malachite green for 20–30 seconds.</li>
<li>Wash in water.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in neutral balsam or DPX.</li>
</ol>
<p>Results
Acid fast bacilli : red
Cells and nuclei : blue or green
Other bacteria : blue or green
Red blood cells : slight reddish tint</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Under the Health and Safety regulations, the practice of flaming is no longer permitted.</li>
<li>Many workers prefer to decolourise with 3% acid-alcohol.</li>
<li>For non-alcohol fast bacteria, 1% aqueous sulphuric acid (H₂SO₄) is used for decolourisation.</li>
<li>A known positive control slide should be stained along with new sections to indicate if the staining procedure is satisfactory.</li>
</ol>
<p>The tubercle bacilli are more resistant than the Mycobacterium leprae so that decolourisation for M. leprae should be more carefully controlled. A faint residual pink colour in the tissues is important. The combination (or the variant of each) of the modification methods of Ziehl Meelsen’s method by Fite, Faraco and Wade is very suitable for leprosy bacilli.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fite-faraco-wade-stain-for-acid-fast-bacilli">Fite-Faraco-Wade Stain for Acid Fast Bacilli<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fite-faraco-wade-stain-for-acid-fast-bacilli" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this method, the paraffin wax is removed from the sections with a mixture of paraffin oil (liquid petroleum) and aviation gasoline, or a mixture of paraffin oil and rectified turpentine, or a mixture of xylene and peanut oil or cotton seed oil or olive oil.</p>
<p>Method</p>
<ol>
<li>Deparaffinise by immersing slide for 1–2 minutes in a mixture of 1 part paraffin oil and 2 parts aviation gasoline, or of 1 part paraffin oil and 2 parts rectified turpentine, or equal parts xylene and peanut oil.</li>
<li>Drain, wipe excess oil from edges, and blot to opacity. Place in water until ready to stain.</li>
<li>Stain with carbol fuchsin for 20–30 minutes at room temperature.</li>
<li>Rinse in water.</li>
<li>Decolourise in 1% acid alcohol until the section is faint pink (1–2 minutes).</li>
<li>Wash in water.</li>
<li>Counterstain with 0.5% methylene blue for 10–15 seconds.</li>
<li>Wash in water, wipe edges clean, blot and then allow to thoroughly dry in air.</li>
<li>Mount in a synthetic mounting medium.</li>
</ol>
<p>Results
Acid fast bacilli : red
Background : blue</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>If M. leprae is being stained, use 0.5% to 1% aqueous sulphuric acid (H₂SO₄) to decolourise.</li>
<li>It is important to blot slide well to prevent residual oil on the slide from producing a staining artefact.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Staining of Microorganisms in Tissues 475</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staining-methods-for-spirochaetes">STAINING METHODS FOR SPIROCHAETES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-methods-for-spirochaetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Spirochaetes are most often looked for in smears of blood and exudates. Some of them such as <em>Borrelia recurrentis</em> which causes relapsing fever, can be seen by high power objective with direct illumination. Many others are stained by Leishman’s and Giemsa’s stains (which are haematology stains).</p>
<p>The best method of detecting spirochaetes in films and to some extent in sections, is the dark ground illumination. The method is most valuable for the examination of syphilitic specimens. The microscope must be set up as described in Section I Chapter 3.</p>
<p>Most of the methods in histopathology for demonstrating spirochaetes are based on silver impregnation techniques.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hage-fontana-silver-method">Hage-Fontana Silver Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hage-fontana-silver-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a silver impregnation method which very good for the detection of spirochaetes in smears.</p>
<p><strong>Fixation</strong> Make thin smear of the suspected material and allow to dry in air.
Fix in Ruge’s fluid</p>
<p><strong>Ruge’s fluid</strong>
Concentrated formaldehyde (40%) 20 ml
Glacial acetic acid 1 ml
Distilled water 100 ml
Fixation time is 1–2 minutes</p>
<p><strong>Mordant</strong>
Phenol 1 g
Tannic acid 5 g
Distilled water 100 ml</p>
<p><strong>Method</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Remove smear from the fixative and wash briefly in running tap water for 10 seconds.</li>
<li>Flood slide with mordant and warm over a flame until steam just rises, leave for 20–30 seconds.</li>
<li>Wash in running tap water for about 30 seconds, then rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Flood slide with 0.25% aqueous silver nitrate and add 1 drop of concentrated ammonia. Warm over a flame for 20–30 seconds. A brownish green colour should form.</li>
<li>Rinse well in distilled water.</li>
<li>Blot and examine dry.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong>
Spirochaetes : black
Background : yellow</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining-spirochaetes-in-sections">Staining Spirochaetes in Sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-spirochaetes-in-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aff958ff">Levaditi’s silver Impregnation method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aff958ff" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is another silver impregnation method but the big disadvantage of this method is that spirochaetes are stained in the tissue blocks. However, it is a reliable method. It does not stain connective tissue, and the spirochaetes appear larger than they really are.</p>
<p><strong>Method</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Wash the tissue for several hours in running water following a 24 hour fixation in formal saline</li>
<li>Transfer to 95% alcohol for 24 hours.</li>
<li>Place in distilled water until the tissue sinks.</li>
<li>Impregnate with 2% aqueous silver nitrate for 3–5 days in the dark at 37 °C.</li>
<li>Wash well in several changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Reduce in 1% hydroquinone in 50% alcohol for 12–24 hours.</li>
<li>Complete dehydration in several changes of ascending grades of alcohol.</li>
<li>Clear in cedar wood oil and embed in paraffin.</li>
<li>Cut sections at 5 μm. Remove the wax with xylene and mount.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong>
Spirochaetes : black
Tissues : yellow or light brown</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Remove all traces of formalin before impregnation with silver nitrate takes place.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>476 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Wash thoroughly before treatment with hydroquinone to avoid precipitation of silver in the tissues as well as on the spirochaetes.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="warthin-starry-method">Warthin-Starry method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#warthin-starry-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is one of the new methods that have replaced the Levaditi’s method because they act on sections instead of tissue blocks. The principle of this method is based on the fact that spirochaetes are argyrophilic, which means that they will absorb silver from a silver solution, but need a separate reducing agent in solution to reduce the adsorbed silver to visible metallic silver. In this case, the reducing agent is a phenolic compound that is oxidised to a quinone during the reduction of silver to metallic silver.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Phosphate buffer (or acidified triply distilled water of pH 4.0).</li>
<li>2% silver nitrate solution (for developer)
Silver nitrate 2 g
Phosphate buffer 100 ml</li>
<li>1% silver nitrate solution (for impregnation)
Silver nitrate 1 g
Phosphate buffer 100 ml</li>
<li>0.15% hydroquinone solution
Hydroquinone (Photographic quality) 0.15 g
Phosphate buffer 100 ml</li>
<li>5% gelatin solution
Select gelatin of high degree of purity 10 g
Warm phosphate buffer 200 ml</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to doubly distilled water.</li>
<li>Rinse twice in doubly distilled water.</li>
<li>Place in 1% silver nitrate solution for 30 minutes at 43°C.</li>
<li>Into separate acid cleaned flasks, add the following solutions: 2% silver nitrate, 5% gelatin, 0.15% hydroquinone. The flasks should be warmed to 56°C.</li>
<li>Prepare the developer solution. The constituents of the developer should be added in the order given and the flask rotated after each addition:</li>
</ol>
<p>2% silver nitrate in phosphate buffer
5% gelatin in phosphate buffer
0.15% hydroquinone
1.5 ml
3.75 ml
2.0 ml
6. Place the slides on a staining rack and cover with the developer. Allow the sections to develop until they are light golden brown or yellow. This may take up to 12 minutes.
7. Rinse rapidly and thoroughly in hot tap water (56°C).
8. Rinse in distilled water.
9. Dehydrate in 95% alcohol and absolute ethanol, clear and mount in synthetic medium.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Spirochaetes : black
Background : pale yellow to light brown</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Include a known positive control slide in each batch.</li>
<li>Development of colour is very critical as underdeveloped section shows the spirochaetes as yellow.</li>
<li>Some substances such as melanin, nuclei and certain pigments have greater affinity for silver than the spirochaetes. Other staining methods which are useful for the detection of spirochaetes in sections include the modification of Dieterie method for spirochaetes and the Steiner and Steiner method, both of which, in addition, stain Legionella pneumophila (causative agent of Legionnaire’s disease) and Negri bodies. As far as the detection of spirochaetes is concerned, these two methods have no particular advantage over the Warthin-Starry method.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6bbf9a12">♦ STAINING METHODS FOR FUNGI IN SECTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6bbf9a12" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ordinary routine haematoxylin and eosin stain most fungi sufficiently enough for them to be rec</p>

<p>Shake to dissolve a white precipitate that forms. Filter this solution into a brown bottle. The clear solution can keep for several months when refrigerated.</p>

5% borax solution 2 ml

<p>Procedure</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Bring sections to distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oxidise in 5% chromic acid for 1 hour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in running tap water for a few seconds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in 1% sodium bisulphite for 1 minute to remove excess residual chromic acid.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in tap water for 10 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in four changes of distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place in freshly prepared methenamine silver nitrate working solution in oven at 58 °C for 45–60 minutes or until the section is yellow brown. Using paraffin coated forceps, remove the control slide, rinse in warm distilled water, and check microscopically for adequate silver impregnation. Fungi should be dark brown. Rinse in distilled water and return to the silver solution if the section is too pale.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in six changes of distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tone in 0.1% gold chloride for 2–5 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treat with 2% sodium thiosulphate solution for 2–5 minutes to remove unreduced silver.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash thoroughly in tap water for five minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counterstain with light green solution for 30 seconds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dehydrate, clear in xylene and mount in a synthetic resin medium.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Results
Fungi : sharply outlined in black
Mucin : grey
Background : pale green</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
