<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining-and-impregnation-methods-for-demonstrating-cns-structures">STAINING AND IMPREGNATION METHODS FOR DEMONSTRATING CNS STRUCTURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-and-impregnation-methods-for-demonstrating-cns-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="nissl-substance">Nissl Substance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nissl-substance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The form, size and distribution of Nissl substance vary in different types of neurones. Because of their rich content of ribonucleic acid (RNA), they are well stained by basic aniline dyes, e.g., thionin, azure A and Cresyl echt violet. The loss of Nissl substance during neuronal injury or disease is called ‘chromatolysis’, and it is a valuable means of microscopically assessing the physiological status of the nerve cells. In the same way, the reappearance of the granules is indication of recovery of functions and conduction of the neurone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thionin-stain-for-nissl-substance-in-paraffin-section">Thionin Stain for Nissl Substance in Paraffin Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thionin-stain-for-nissl-substance-in-paraffin-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Thionin stain</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Thionin 0.5 g</li>
<li>Distilled water 100 ml</li>
<li>Acetic acid 2 drops</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Differentiating solution</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Lute alcohol and 1,4-dioxane. Equal parts of thionin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Take section through xylene, dioxane and distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in thionin solution for five minutes.</li>
<li>Differentiate until practically colourless in the differentiating solution.</li>
<li>Pass through two changes of dioxane.</li>
<li>Rinse in two changes of xylene.</li>
<li>Mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Nissl substance : bright blue
Background : colourless.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>
&gt; 1. For differentiation, Gothard’s mixture of cajput oil 40 ml, xylene 50 ml, pure creosote 50 ml and absolute alcohol 160 ml, can also be used.
&gt; 2. Never place stained sections in water or alcohol before or after differentiation as both will remove the stain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cresyl-echt-violet-for-nissl-substance-in-paraffin-section">Cresyl Echt Violet for Nissl Substance in Paraffin Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cresyl-echt-violet-for-nissl-substance-in-paraffin-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Cresyl echt violet
0.5% aqueous solution of cresyl echt violet ripened for 24–48 hours. Filter before use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Balsam xylene solution
Equal parts of Canada balsam and xylene.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Bring section to distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in cresyl echt violet solution for five minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in two changes of distilled water.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>The Central Nervous System (CNS) 493</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Rinse in 95% alcohol for 30 seconds.</li>
<li>Rinse in absolute alcohol for 30 seconds.</li>
<li>Rinse in xylene for one minute.</li>
<li>Rinse in balsam xylene mixture for two minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in two changes of absolute alcohol for 10–30 seconds.</li>
<li>Wash in 3–4 changes of xylene.</li>
<li>Mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Nissl substance : blue</p>
<table><thead><tr><th><strong>Note</strong></th><th>Steps 7–9 may have to be repeated several times.</th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="demonstration-of-neurones-axons-dendrites-and-neurofibrils">Demonstration of Neurones, Axons, Dendrites and Neurofibrils<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demonstration-of-neurones-axons-dendrites-and-neurofibrils" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Axons and dendrites are the two processes that originate from the cell body of the neurones. Dendrites, which are usually short and have many branches, lack myelin sheaths. They contain both Nissl substance and neurofibrils. Axons carry nerve impulses over a long distance. They terminate either on the dendrites or cell body of other neurones, thus forming a synapse, or end on special sites associated with an effector organ such as muscles or glands. The axon contains neurofibrils but no Nissl substance.</p>
<p>Neurofibrils are present in the cytoplasm of the cell body, axon and dendrites. Silver impregnation methods are utilised to demonstrate nerve fibres and neurofibrils, though most of these methods are capricious. They are invaluable for the study of CNS because of the clarity of images produced by them. They give a thick black impregnation of nerve cells and their processes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="golgi-cox-potassium-dichromate-mercuric-chloride-method">Golgi-Cox Potassium Dichromate-Mercuric Chloride Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#golgi-cox-potassium-dichromate-mercuric-chloride-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a modification of the original Golgi method of 1878. Though still widely used by many laboratories because of its reliability, it is being superseded by other faster methods. The method is based on the treatment of pieces of central nervous system with potassium dichromate, followed by impregnation with silver nitrate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fixation">Fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Golgi - Cox solution</strong></p>
<p>5% potassium dichromate 10 volumes
5% mercuric chloride 10 volumes
5% potassium chromate 8 volumes
Distilled water 15–20 volumes</p>
<p>Mix the potassium dichromate and the mercuric chloride together, and the potassium chromate with the distilled water and then mix the two solutions. Use the fixative at 37 °C.</p>
<p>Place the tissue on a layer of glass wool in 20 times its volume of fixative solution. Change the fixative after 24 and 48 hours incubation. Then seal the container and keep in the dark at 37 °C for about 1–2 months.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="preparation-of-sections">Preparation of sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>After sufficient impregnation, soak the block in 20% solution of neutral dextrin for 1–3 days. Embed in celloidin. With the freezing microtome, cut section at 50 μm–100 μm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="staining-method">Staining method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Place the sections in 5% sodium carbonate for 1 hour in order to blacken the impregnation.</li>
<li>Wash well in distilled water.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in graded alcohols.</li>
<li>Clear in creosote for a few minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer to turpentine.</li>
<li>Mount in synthetic resin.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Nerve cells : black
Axon : black
Dendrites : black
Neuroglia : black</p>
<p>|  <strong>Note</strong> | 1. In step 1, 5–10% ammonia solution can also be used.
2. In addition to the above results, blood vessels may also be impregnated.  |
| --- | --- |</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>494 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bielschowsky-s-method-for-axons-and-neurofibrils">Bielschowsky's Method for Axons and Neurofibrils<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bielschowsky-s-method-for-axons-and-neurofibrils" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>2% aqueous silver nitrate.</li>
<li>Ammoniacal silver
40% freshly prepared aqueous solution of sodium hydroxide
10% aqueous silver nitrate
Concentrated ammonium hydroxide
Distilled water
Slowly add five drops of the sodium hydroxide to 10 ml of the silver nitrate. This results in the formation of a black brown precipitate. The precipitate is dissolved by adding ammonium hydroxide dropwise, shaking well after each drop. Not more than 18 drops are to be used. Then add 10 ml distilled water to give a final volume of 20 ml.</li>
<li>Aqueous gold chloride
Add 3–5 drops of 1% gold chloride to 10 ml of distilled water (0.2% aqueous gold chloride).</li>
<li>5% aqueous sodium thiosulphate.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Formalin fixed tissue block (3–6 weeks in formalin) are cut into thin slices of tissue and washed in running tap water for 24 hours, followed by several changes of distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cut thin frozen sections and place in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Immerse in 2% silver nitrate until brown for about 18–24 hours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash briefly in distilled water</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place in ammoniacal silver solution until deep brown (about 10–15 minutes).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in several changes of distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place in 10% formalin and transfer quickly to fresh formalin solution for 15–20 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash well in tap water, followed by distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tone in 0.2% gold chloride until sections are grey (about 10–40 minutes).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Remove unreduced silver by treatment with 5% sodium thiosulphate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in distilled water (counterstain model with neutral red or safranin if desired).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mount sections on slide in aqueous mixing medium, or dehydrate in ascending grades of alcohol, clear in xylene and mount in synthetic resin medium.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Neurofibrils, axons and dendrites : black
Background : greyish</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>
&gt; 1. It is always advisable to take several sections from each block for this method and other metallic impregnation methods. One of these sections may likely show superior impregnation.
&gt; 2. Lack of toning with gold chloride usually gives black nerve fibres and a golden brown background. Two or three drops of glacial acetic acid added to toning bath will result in purplish background.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="holme-s-method-for-axons">Holme's Method for Axons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#holme-s-method-for-axons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is a modification of the Bodian copper Protargol method, and it gives more consistent and reliable results on formalin-fixed tissues. Protargol, a silver proteinate in the Bordian stain, never reaches the optimal impregnation. Holmes developed a buffered impregnating solution so that the specificity of the stain is determined during impregnation by the effect of the solution pH and the concentration of silver ions.</p>
<p>This method is useful for paraffin sections of both central and peripheral nervous system tissues. Ten per cent neutral buffered formalin is the fixative of choice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>20% aqueous silver nitrate.</li>
<li>1% aqueous silver nitrate.</li>
<li>10% pyridine.</li>
<li>Boric acid buffer solution
Boric acid</li>
</ol>
<p>1.24 g
Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>The Central Nervous System (CNS) 495</p>
<p>Distilled water 100 ml
5. Borax buffer solution
Sodium borate (borax) 1.9 g
Distilled water 100 ml
6. Impregnating solution
Boric acid buffer solution 27.5 ml
Borax buffer solution 27.5 ml
Distilled water 257 ml
1% silver nitrate solution 0.5 ml
10% pyridine 2.5 ml
7. Reducing solution
Hydroquinone 1 g
Sodium sulphite crystals 10 g
Distilled water 100 ml
This solution is stable for only two days.
8. 0.2% gold chloride solution.
9. 2% oxalic acid solution.</p>
<p><strong>Procedure</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Take sections through xylene.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Transfer to absolute alcohol</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Transfer to 95% alcohol.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hydrate in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place sections in 20% silver nitrate solution for 1–2 hours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in three changes of distilled water for 10 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place sections in impregnating solution in a covered jar in at least 20 ml of solution per slide. Incubate at 37°C overnight.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Remove slides, drain excess solution and place in reducing solution for at least two minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in running tap water for three minutes and then rinse in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tone in gold chloride for three minutes. (Continue beyond three minutes if sections are still brown).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place in oxalic acid for 3–10 minutes, examine microscopically at intervals until the axons are thoroughly blue-black.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place in sodium thiosulphate to fix for five minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash in running water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counterstain nuclei if desired, with neutral red.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong>
Axons and neurofibrils : blue black
Background : greyish</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Best results are produced following mercuric chloride fixation.</li>
<li>Frozen and cellulose nitrate sections can also be impregnated.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>NEUROGLIA</strong></p>
<p>Neuroglial cells provide the internal support for the central nervous system. They form the connective tissue of the CNS, and could be referred to as the ‘Nerve glue’. Four types of cells make up the glia—astrocytes, oligodendroglia, microglia and ependymal cells.</p>
<p>Astrocytes are stellate cells and they are in two forms: protoplasmic, which are found in the grey matter, and fibrous which occur in the white matter. They provide a support for tracts of nerve fibres and also take part in fluid, gas and metabolite exchanges between nervous tissue, blood and cerebrospinal fluid. After tissue injury or trauma, by proliferation of their processes, they participate in the formation of gliosis.</p>
<p>Oligodendroglia occur in both the grey matter and the white matter. They are small cells (smaller than astrocytes). Their primary function in the CNS is their involvement in the formation and perhaps maintenance of myelin sheath. They do not form fibres and their small nuclei are clearly visible in haematoxylin and eosin stained sections.</p>
<p>Microglia are mesodermal in origin, unlike the astrocytes and oligodendroglia that are ectodermal. They are fixed ‘scavenger’ cells which are found throughout the brain and the spinal cord.</p>
<p>Ependymal cells occur along the ventricles and the spinal canal. They are epithelial cells and are involved in forming a selective barrier between the cerebrospinal fluid and the nervous tissue.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>496 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<p>To demonstrate neuroglia, it is essential that the tissue is fresh as they are readily affected by autolysis. Several and various impregnation and staining methods are required on paraffin, cellulose nitrate and frozen sections in order to demonstrate all types of neuroglial cells. Some methods are valuable in the study of general cellular distribution and structure of the tissue. These stains make use of basic aniline dyes to stain the DNA of the nucleus and RNA of the Nissl substance and the nucleoli; and require an experienced histotechnologist for proper interpretation of the staining reactions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="toluidine-blue-for-nerve-cells-and-glia">Toluidine Blue for Nerve Cells and Glia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toluidine-blue-for-nerve-cells-and-glia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fixation in alcohol gives the best result but formalin serves well too.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<li>
<p>Alcoholic colophonium solution
Colophonium (resin) 10 g
95% alcohol 100 ml</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Toluidine blue stain
Toluidine blue 0.1 g
Distilled water 100 ml</p>
</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Pass the paraffin section through xylene, absolute alcohol and 95% alcohol.</li>
<li>Place slides in alcoholic colophonium solution for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in two changes of 95% alcohol for three minutes each.</li>
<li>Stain with toluidine blue for 30 seconds.</li>
<li>Differentiate in aniline-alcohol until the background is clear.</li>
<li>Rinse in oil of cajput until clear.</li>
<li>Clear in two changes of xylene.</li>
<li>Mount in synthetic resin.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Nerve Cells
Nucleus : pale blue
Nissl substance : dark blue</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="glia">Glia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Astrocytes : pale blue
Oligodendroglia : very dark blue</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cajal-s-gold-chloride-sublimate-method-for-astrocytes-cajal-ramon-1913">Cajal's Gold Chloride-Sublimate Method for Astrocytes (Cajal &amp; Ramon, 1913)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cajal-s-gold-chloride-sublimate-method-for-astrocytes-cajal-ramon-1913" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a gold impregnation method that selectively stains astrocytes, and it is performed on frozen sections. Fixation is in Cajal’s formalin-ammonium bromide mixture (FAB) and it should last no less than two days and not more than 25 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Formalin-ammonium bromide solution
Ammonium bromide 15 g
40% formaldehyde 100 ml
Distilled water 400 ml</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gold sublimate solution
1% gold chloride (brown gold chloride) 5 ml
1% mercuric chloride 25 ml
Distilled water 5 ml</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>5% aqueous solution of sodium thiosulphate</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Wash sections in three changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in the gold sublimate solution in a covered dish in the dark for 4–6 hours at room temperature. Use 15 ml of fluid for each section. Check impregnation microscopically until deep purple.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Place in 5% sodium thiosulphate to fix for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash thoroughly in distilled water.</li>
<li>Rinse in 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Mount sections on slides, blot with fluffless paper.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results-astrocytes-opaque-purplish-black">Results Astrocytes: opaque purplish-black<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results-astrocytes-opaque-purplish-black" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phosphotungstic-acid-haematoxylin-ptah-mallory-s-modification">Phosphotungstic Acid-Haematoxylin (PTAH) (Mallory's Modification)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phosphotungstic-acid-haematoxylin-ptah-mallory-s-modification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method which was described for connective tissue, stains glial fibres more satisfactorily when</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>The Central Nervous System (CNS) 497</p>
<p>slightly modified. For glial fibres, decolourisation with sodium thiosulphate is missed. This method which is particularly useful for the demonstration of hyperplasia and hypertrophy of fibrous astrocytes, can be used with paraffin or cellulose nitrate sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>1% potassium permanganate</li>
<li>5% oxalic acid</li>
<li>Phosphotungstic acid-haematoxylin (PTAH)
Haematoxylin 1 g
Phosphotungstic acid 20 g
Distilled water 1000 ml</li>
</ol>
<p>Dissolve the haematoxylin in one half of the distilled water with the aid of gentle heat, and the phosphotungstic acid in the other half, then mix the two. Natural ripening requires several weeks, but the addition of 0.2 g of potassium permanganate ripens the stain at once and makes it ready for use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take sections to distilled water.</li>
<li>Mordant sections in Zenker's fluid with acetic acid overnight at room temperature or 1 hour at 50 °C. Alternatively, mordant in saturated aqueous mercuric chloride for 20–30 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running water for 15 minutes.</li>
<li>Place in Lugol’s iodine for 15 minutes.</li>
<li>Decolourise in 95% alcohol for at least one hour.</li>
<li>Rinse in three changes of distilled water.</li>
<li>Place in potassium permanganate to oxidise for 15–20 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running water for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer to 5% oxalic acid to decolourise for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running water for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse briefly in distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in PTAH solution for 12–18 hours.</li>
<li>Dip quickly in 95% alcohol for one minute.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Astrocytes : blue</p>
<p>Nuclei : blue
Fibrin : blue
Myelin : blue
Collagen : rose or brick red</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="myelin">MYELIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myelin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Myelin is the white fatty material that forms an ‘insulation’ for the nerve fibres. The myelin is formed by the Schwann cells in the peripheral nervous system and oligodendroglia in the central nervous system. It consists of a mixture of lipids and proteins.</p>
<p>Most methods for demonstrating myelin, except Luxol fast blue, work almost on the same principle: Mordant-haematoxylin complex attaches to the phospholipid component of the myelin sheath, which has an affinity for the dye lake. Differentiation is in two parts—the first removes excess dye lake while the second stage confines the lake to desired site.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="f489bf62">Weil’s Haematoxylin Method for Myelin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f489bf62" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a regressive staining method in which the sections are initially overstained and then differentiated in two stages. Formalin fixed tissue with or without a chrome salt mordanting is used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Ferric ammonium sulphate solution
4% aqueous solution of ferric ammonium sulphate.</li>
<li>Haematoxylin solution
1% solution of haematoxylin - add 90 ml of distilled water to 10 ml of 10% solution of haematoxylin in absolute alcohol.</li>
<li>Staining solution
Mix equal parts of 4% ferric ammonium sulphate and 1% haematoxylin just before use. Use this mixture only once.</li>
<li>Differentiating solution
Borax (sodium borate) 10 g
Potassium ferricyanide 12.5 g
Distilled water 1000 ml</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>498 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Remove wax with xylene and take section to distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain in the 1% iron haematoxylin at room temperature for 20–30 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running water.</li>
<li>Differentiate in 4% ferric ammonium sulphate until stain is removed from the back of the paraffin section.</li>
<li>Wash well in running water.</li>
<li>Complete differentiation in borax ferricyanide until nuclei are barely visible microscopically.</li>
<li>Wash in two changes of tap water.</li>
<li>Wash in dilute ammonia water (6 drops of ammonium hydroxide to 100 ml of water).</li>
<li>Wash in distilled water.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Myelin sheath: blue to blue black
Red blood cells: very black
Nuclei: dark grey</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="osmium-tetroxide-method">Osmium Tetroxide Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#osmium-tetroxide-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This simple method is very useful for the demonstration of normal and degenerating myelin. The use of osmium tetroxide is however, hazardous and costly. Fresh or formalin fixed tissue may be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Place small pieces of tissue in 0.5 to 1% osmium tetroxide in distilled water for 3–7 days.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash thoroughly in water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Either cut frozen section, or take section to paraffin wax.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For paraffin section, treat with 70% alcohol for 12–24 hours. This promotes secondary blackening of some fatty substances and renders the ‘osmicated’ myelin resistant to higher grades of alcohol.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treat with alcohol, and clear with chloroform (the preferred clearing agent). Wax briefly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dry the section with gentle heat.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mount section directly if so desired, with synthetic resin medium, or take to water and counter stain.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Healthy myelin: black or dark grey
Degenerating myelin: black granular deposits</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>: If a dark background is produced as a result of over-reduction, then treat sections with potassium permanganate, followed by oxalic acid, and clear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pal-weigert-method-for-myelin">Pal-Weigert Method for Myelin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pal-weigert-method-for-myelin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The staining mixture (haematoxylin and lithium carbonate) forms a lake with the tissue components. Potassium permanganate is used for the first differentiation and also aids in confining the action of the dye lake on the myelin sheath and red blood cells. Pal’s bleach is used for the second and final differentiation. Oxalic acid removes excess permanganate from the section.</p>
<p>Celloidin, paraffin or frozen sections in this order of preference may be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Mordanting solution</strong>
4% aqueous ferric ammonium sulphate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Staining solution</strong></p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Solution A</strong>
| Saturated aqueous lithium carbonate | 7 ml |
| Distilled water | 93 ml |</p>
<p><strong>Solution B</strong>
| Haematoxylin | 1 g |
| Absolute alcohol | 10 ml |</p>
<p>This solution does not require ripening.
For use, add 1 volume of solution A to 9 volumes of solution B.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p><strong>Differentiating solution</strong>
0.4% aqueous potassium permanganate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Decoloursing solution</strong>
| Oxalic acid | 1 g |
| Sodium sulphite | 1 g |
| Distilled water | 1000 ml |</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>This is to be prepared just before use.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>The Central Nervous System (CNS) 499</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Place sections in mordanting solution for 2–24 hours.</li>
<li>Wash in tap water.</li>
<li>Stain in the staining solution for 1–3 hours.</li>
<li>Wash in tap water for 3 minutes.</li>
<li>Place in mordanting solution to partially decolourise until the grey and white matter are barely distinguishable. (The time varies).</li>
<li>Wash in tap water for three minutes.</li>
<li>Differentiate in 0.4% potassium permanganate until the grey and white matter are clearly visible when sections are held up to the light.</li>
<li>Rinse briefly in tap water.</li>
<li>Completely decolourise by placing section in the decolourising solution. The grey matter should become completely clear and colourless, except where some myelinated fibres exist.</li>
<li>Wash in tap water for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in solution A to restore the blue colour lost during decolourisation for five minutes.</li>
<li>Wash thoroughly in tap water.</li>
<li>Counterstain if desired with neutral red.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Myelin sheaths : dark blue
Other structures : unstained, except if counterstained</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>This method is Pal’s modification of the original Weigert’s haematoxylin method.</li>
<li>Some workers first treat formalin-fixed material with Weigerts primary mordant (po-tassium dichromate 5 g, chromium fluoride 2 g, dissolved by boiling in 100 ml distilled water) for 5 days.</li>
<li>Kultschitsky modified Weigerts method by making use of acidified haematoxylin (2 ml glacial acetic acid added to 100 ml alcoholic solution of 1% haematoxylin).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="luxol-fast-blue-method-for-myelin">Luxol Fast Blue Method for Myelin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#luxol-fast-blue-method-for-myelin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Luxol fast blue is a dye of the sulphonated copper phthalocyanine type that is alcohol soluble. It has affinity for phospholipid of myelin. Ten per cent formal-saline is fixative of choice. Paraffin, cellulose nitrate or frozen sections may be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="solution">Solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Luxol fast blue MBS or
methasol fast blue 2G 0.1 g
10% acetic acid 0.5 ml
95% alcohol 100 ml
Filter. The stain keeps for up to 1 year</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Remove wax with xylene.</li>
<li>Take sections to absolute alcohol.</li>
<li>Stain in Luxol fast blue or methasol fast blue for 10–20 hours.</li>
<li>Rinse in 0.05% lithium carbonate for only 3–5 seconds. This is initial differentiation.</li>
<li>Continue differentiation in 70% alcohol for 20–30 seconds.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water. Repeat steps 4, 5 and 6 if necessary until the difference between the blue staining white matter and the colourless grey matter is clear.</li>
<li>Wash thoroughly in distilled water.</li>
<li>Counterstain either in 0.2% cresyl fast violet or 1% neutral red for 10 to 20 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Differentiate the counterstain in 95% alcohol.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Myelin : deep purplish blue
Erythrocytes : deep purplish blue
Nuclei : purplish-blue (or red depending on the counterstain used)
Nissl substance : purplish-blue (or red depending on the counterstain used)</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>500 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="luxol-fast-blue-combination-methods">Luxol Fast Blue Combination Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#luxol-fast-blue-combination-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The combination of Luxol fast blue method with a variety of common staining methods provides the most useful and reliable method for the demonstration of pathological processes in the CNS. The common staining methods include the periodic acid-Schiff, oil red O, phosphotungstic acid haematoxylin and Holmes silver nitrate methods. The combination of Luxol fast blue and oil red O is described below:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="luxol-fast-blue-oil-red-o">Luxol fast blue-oil red O<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#luxol-fast-blue-oil-red-o" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method demonstrates fat as well as myelin. Ten per cent neutral buffered formalin is the fixative of choice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Luxol fast blue</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Luxol fast blue MBS 1 g</li>
<li>70% alcohol 100 ml</li>
<li>10% acetic acid 0.5 ml</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Oil red O</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Oil red O 0.4 g</li>
<li>Acetone 10 ml</li>
<li>Mix well and then add 80% alcohol 90 ml</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>0.005% lithium carbonate in distilled water</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>0.5% acid-alcohol</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Hydrochloric acid 0.5 ml</li>
<li>50% alcohol 100 ml</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Harris haematoxylin</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Cut frozen sections at 10–20 μm and place in tap water.</li>
<li>Take sections through 50% and 70% alcohols.</li>
<li>Stain in Luxol fast blue at room temperature for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse briefly in 70% alcohol.</li>
<li>Pass quickly through 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Place sections in distilled water containing a few drops of 95% alcohol to control surface tension.</li>
<li>Place in the 0.005% lithium carbonate for 20–30 seconds.</li>
<li>Place in 70% alcohol for 15–20 seconds.</li>
<li>Take sections through 50% alcohol to distilled water containing a few drops of 95% alcohol. Repeat steps 7 and 8 if further decolourisation is needed.</li>
<li>Wash in distilled water for three minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse briefly in 70% alcohol.</li>
<li>Stain section in oil red O for 20–30 seconds.</li>
<li>Pass section rapidly through 70% alcohol and then 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water for two minutes.</li>
<li>Stain with Harris haematoxylin for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water for two minutes.</li>
<li>Decolourise briefly in acid alcohol and then dip briefly in 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Wash in distilled water.</li>
<li>Blue in lithium carbonate.</li>
<li>Dip in 70% alcohol.</li>
<li>Dip in 50% alcohol.</li>
<li>Rinse in tap water.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerol gelatin or other neutral aqueous mounting medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Fat : red
Myelin sheath : blue</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Chapter 14</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="enzyme-histochemistry">Enzyme Histochemistry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enzyme-histochemistry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When histology and biochemistry come together, the science is known as Histochemistry. This branch of science aims at identifying chemical substances and determine their significance at the cellular level. Enzyme histochemistry is therefore a sub-division of this field that specifically deals with enzymes.</p>
<p>Enzymes are catalysts that speed up chemical reactions that occur in living cells. In addition to accelerating reactions, enzymes are highly specific in their activity. They act on specific substrates—the active reagents that must be present for enzyme activity to occur. In ordinary histological demonstration, there is a direct interaction between the tissue constituents in the section and a dye or reagent to produce visible colouration of the tissue. With enzyme histochemistry, the final opaque or coloured product is derived from the substrate rather than the tissue. Enzymes are very unstable and almost all of them disappear from the tissues quickly and progressively after removal of tissue from the body and after cellular death. Many of them are simply dissolved in the cell cytoplasm (soluble enzymes) and others are tightly attached to certain cell organelles such as mitochondria and lysosomes. Special precautions are necessary to preserve them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-affecting-enzyme-demonstration">FACTORS AFFECTING ENZYME DEMONSTRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-affecting-enzyme-demonstration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The factors that influence enzyme demonstration should well be borne in mind in order to successfully identify the enzymes and determine their significance. The following factors affect enzyme demonstration:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Optimal temperature Optimal temperature is one at which maximal enzyme activity is achieved. Most enzymes require incubation at temperatures between 25 °C and 37 °C.</li>
<li>Optimal pH Maximal enzyme activity will occur at an optimal pH level. In majority of cases, this pH level is close to the neutral on the pH scale. The optimal pH may vary according to the substrate used.</li>
<li>Concentration The speed of enzyme reaction is greatly influenced by the amount (concentration) of the enzyme, the substrate, and of the reaction product.</li>
<li>Inhibitors Enzyme activity is affected by the presence of inhibitors. Some inhibitors are specific when they are capable of affecting only particular enzymes; or non specific when they do act on nearly all the enzymes.</li>
<li>Activators These are substances that further enhance enzyme activity.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>502 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specimen-preparation-for-enzyme-histochemistry">SPECIMEN PREPARATION FOR ENZYME HISTOCHEMISTRY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specimen-preparation-for-enzyme-histochemistry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Histochemical methods for enzymes have played a great role in the identification and evaluation of enzyme activity. Many specimen preparations have been tried and used over the years until the arrival of refrigerated microtome (cryostat). The important aim always is that tissue must be prepared in such a way as to preserve and retain the enzymes as much as possible in their original sites. Enzymes should not deteriorate or diffuse during fixation and the final colour reaction should be sharp and precise. Fresh frozen (cryostat) sections have almost completely superseded sections of freeze-dried tissue, tissue that has been fixed in conventional fixatives and sectioned on carbon dioxide freezing microtome; or fixed tissues embedded in paraffin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fresh-tissue-preparations">Fresh Tissue Preparations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fresh-tissue-preparations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fresh unfixed tissue may be frozen by the cryostat freezer plate method, or the liquid nitrogen immersion method or by the pre-chilled isopentane method which is particularly suitable for muscle tissue. Within 3 or 4 minutes of obtaining fresh tissue, cryostat sections can be prepared and introduced into the substrate solution thus bypassing the complicated and prolonged processing. This method of tissue preparation for enzyme demonstration is fast and easy to handle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fixed-tissue-preparations">Fixed Tissue Preparations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixed-tissue-preparations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some soluble enzymes survive fixation to the extent that sufficient amounts of the enzyme is retained for demonstration. Fixed tissues tend to show just few diffusion artefacts. Ice-cold acetone is the fixative of choice, alternatively ice-cold alcohol or formalin or ice-cold formal-calcium can be used. Paraffin embedding must be brief at 56 °C in the vacuum oven. It is also possible to cut frozen sections following complete fixation especially with ice-cold formalin. Also, cryostat sections can be post-fixed for 10–30 minutes in any of the aforementioned ice-cold reagents. This method is particularly useful for such enzymes as the phosphatase and lipases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="freeze-drying-preparations">Freeze-drying Preparations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#freeze-drying-preparations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Freeze-drying is one of the important methods of preparing tissues for enzyme histochemistry. Though the modern freeze-drying equipments are now easier to use and the method effectively preserves enzymes, it is virtually completely superseded by the cryostat method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="controls">Controls<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#controls" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>False negative or false positive reactions can easily occur due to certain factors associated with the general procedures for enzyme demonstration. False-negative reactions may be caused by:</p>
<p>(i) Insufficient amount of enzyme.
(ii) Non-optimal incubation conditions.
(iii) Substrate degeneration.
(iv) Solubility or diffusion of either enzyme or the final product of the enzyme activity.</p>
<p>And false-positive reactions may be due to:</p>
<p>(i) Non-enzymatic splitting of the substrate.
(ii) Diffusion of the enzyme or the final product of enzyme activity away from the initial positive site.
(iii) Non-specific affinity of tissue components for reagents used in the procedure, and
(iv) Confusion of natural pigments with coloured end product of the reaction.</p>
<p>A known positive and a known negative control must be treated in conjunction with the sections under investigation. These controls assist in determining whether procedure results are satisfactory. Negative controls are usually prepared as follows:</p>
<p>(i) The omission of an essential step in the procedure such as the replacement of substrate with distilled water.
(ii) The use of specific inhibitors of enzyme activity.
(iii) The treatment of sections with a non-specific agent known to destroy the enzyme, e.g., boiling water, strong acids, etc.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Enzyme Histochemistry 503</p>
<p>Any positive reaction obtained after the sections have been treated as listed above, suggests that the test is non-specific, and not caused by enzyme activity. The positive reaction observed with the positive control indicates that the reagents are working.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reaction-process-of-enzyme-histochemistry">REACTION PROCESS OF ENZYME HISTOCHEMISTRY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reaction-process-of-enzyme-histochemistry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Most of the enzyme histochemical methods are based on the formation of a primary reaction product (PRP) as a result of the action of the enzyme upon the substrate. Following this, is the production of a coloured or opaque final reaction product (FRP) from the combination of PRP with a second reagent. For example the blackening of the PRP by chemical reaction with a diazonium salt to form a diazo-dye. This is often referred to as azo-dye method. The enzyme activity frees the naphthol moiety on the substrate (containing naphthol compounds), which combines with the diazonium salt. When the production of the PRP and its transformation as a coloured FRP take place at the same time, it is called 'simultaneous coupling'. In a reaction where the two reactions occur one after the other, it is 'post incubation coupling'.</p>
<p>Some procedures employ indoxyl substrates. The enzyme activity results in the release of indoxyl radicals which are then rapidly oxidised to insoluble indigo blue final products. There are other methods that use metal salts when one of the products of enzyme activity is an acid. The released acid is 'captured' by a metal ion in the incubation medium and so precipitated. Additional reagents are used up and ultimately an insoluble coloured salt is formed at the site of enzyme activity. The redox (oxidation–reduction) reaction methods involve the removal of hydrogen from one substance (oxidation) and transferring it to another (reduction). A good number of oxidative enzymes are demonstrated by the methods that depend on the transfer of hydrogen from the substrate to a tetrazolium salt. The tetrazolium salt is then reduced to a water insoluble purple formazan pigment at the site of enzyme activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-enzyme-demonstration">METHODS OF ENZYME DEMONSTRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-enzyme-demonstration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="alkaline-phosphatase">Alkaline Phosphatase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alkaline-phosphatase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The alkaline phosphatase together with acid phosphatase make up the group of enzymes that are now called phosphomonoesterases. These enzymes hydrolyse orthophosphate from their particular substrate. The alkaline phosphatase hydrolyses at alkaline pH while the acid phosphotase does it at acid pH. Alkaline phosphatase is widely distributed in tissues. It is usually activated by certain ions such as magnesium, manganese, zinc and cobalt. It is inhibited by cysteine, cyanides and arsenates. There are several methods for demonstrating alkaline phosphatase, two of which will be described here. The optimum pH for activity is 9.27 but the range is 9.0–9.6.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="azo-dye-coupling-method-for-alkaline-phosphatase">Azo-dye Coupling Method for Alkaline Phosphatase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#azo-dye-coupling-method-for-alkaline-phosphatase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The substrate used in this method is a solution of alpha naphthyl phosphate. The alpha naphthol moiety is released by the enzyme and is coupled with the diazonium salt to form an insoluble coloured final reaction product. Fresh frozen cryostat sections are preferably used but fixed tissues can also be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Dissolve 10–20 mg of sodium alpha-naphthyl phosphate in 20 ml of *TRIS buffer at pH 9.1. Add 20 mg of Fast-Red TR or Fast Black B and stir well. This should be prepared fresh.</li>
</ol>
<p>*TRIS (tris[hydroxymethyl] aminomethane) buffer, pH 9.1:</p>
