<table><thead><tr><th>0.2M TRIS (24.2g/L)</th><th>25 ml</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>0.1N HCl (8.5 ml conc. HCl/L)</td><td>5 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Distilled water</td><td>70 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ol start="2">
<li>Mayer’s haemalum</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>504 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Filter the freshly prepared substrate-diazonium salt on the slides. Leave for 15–60 minutes (Paraffin sections may require up to 12 hours with Fast-Red TR).</li>
<li>Wash in running water for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Counterstain in Mayer’s haemalum for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash and blue nuclei in running water for 20–30 minutes.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The site of enzyme activity: brown with Fast-Red or black with Fast Black B.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indoxyl-method-for-alkaline-phosphatase">Indoxyl Method for Alkaline Phosphatase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indoxyl-method-for-alkaline-phosphatase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When sections are incubated in a buffer containing either iodoindoxyl phosphate or bromoindoxyl phosphate as substrate, orthophosphate and indoxyl derivative are released. The indoxyl derivative is oxidised to insoluble indigo blue to locate the site of enzyme activity.</p>
<p>Fresh or fixed cryostat sections are preferred.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>2 M sodium chloride (117g/L).</li>
<li>Barbital (Veronal) hydrochloric acid buffer, pH 9.0
0.2 N Hydrochloric acid 0.21 ml
0.04 M barbital (Veronal) sodium 12.5 ml</li>
<li>5-iodoindoxyl phosphate or 5 bromoindoxyl phosphate.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Weigh 0.00192 g of 5 iodoindoxyl phosphate or 5 bromoindoxyl phosphate and place in Tube 1.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To Tube 2 add in the following order:
2 M sodium chloride 5 ml
Distilled deionised water 3 ml
Barbital hydrochloric acid buffer 2 ml
Mix well and add to tube 1. Mix.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pour the mixture onto the sections. Incubate at 37 °C for 60 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse sections in distilled water when incubation is over.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counterstain, if desired, in 0.5% safranin O for 30 seconds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rinse thoroughly in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mount using an aqueous mounting medium.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites of enzyme activity: fine precipitates of indigo blue
Nuclei: red, if counterstained with safranin O</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="calcium-phosphate-method-for-alkaline-phosphatase">Calcium Phosphate Method for Alkaline Phosphatase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calcium-phosphate-method-for-alkaline-phosphatase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a fairly popular method. Phosphate ions which are released from the substrate glycerophosphate are precipitated as calcium phosphate. The calcium is then substituted for cobalt and seen as opaque cobalt sulphide. The site of enzyme activity is brownish-black and so also is calcium in the tissue. The method is not specific and must be accompanied by a control section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7d77326">♦ ACID PHOSPHATASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7d77326" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acid phosphatase is the other member of the group, phosphomonoesterases. It hydrolyses orthophosphate at an acid pH. The optimum pH for the enzyme activity is 5.0. It is inhibited by fluoride but not activated by magnesium. Early methods for the demonstration of acid phosphatase were not reliable and were capricious. A lot of improvement has taken place and so today’s methods are as reliable as those of alkaline phosphatase.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indoxyl-method-for-acid-phosphatase">Indoxyl Method for Acid Phosphatase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indoxyl-method-for-acid-phosphatase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When sections are incubated in a buffered medium with 5-iodoindoxyl phosphate or 5-bromoindoxyl phosphate as substrate, the activity of the enzyme at acid pH releases orthophosphate and indoxyl derivatives from the substrates. By the enhancing oxidising action of potassium ferricyanide and potassium ferrocyanide solution, the indoxyl derivatives are changed to insoluble indigo blue precipitates. These indicate the sites of enzyme activity. The potassium ferricyanide and potassium ferrocyanide are additional oxidising agents to improve localisation of the enzymes. Either fresh or</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Enzyme Histochemistry 505</p>
<p>fixed tissue may be used. Cut cryostat sections at 6–8 μm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>2 M sodium chloride</li>
<li>0.1 M citrate buffer pH 5.4
0.1 M citric acid 6.4 ml
0.1 M sodium citrate 13.4 ml</li>
<li>0.05 M potassium ferricyanide.</li>
<li>0.05 M potassium ferrocyanide.</li>
<li>5-iodoindoxyl phosphate or 5-bromoin-doxyl phosphate (sodium salt)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>To tube 1, add 0.00192 g of 5-iodoindoxyl phosphate.</li>
<li>To tube 2, add in the following order:
2 M sodium chloride 5 ml
Distilled deionised water 2 ml
Citrate buffer, pH 5.4 2 ml
Potassium ferricyanide 0.5 ml
Potassium ferrocyanide 0.5 ml</li>
</ol>
<p>Mix very well and add to tube 1. Mix again. Pour the mixture on to the sections.
3. Incubate at 37 °C for 60 minutes.
4. Rinse in distilled water.
5. Counterstain if desired, in 0.5% safranin O for 30 seconds.
6. Rinse thoroughly in distilled water.
7. Coverslip, using an aqueous mounting medium.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites of enzyme activity : fine precipitate of indigo blue
Nuclei : red, if safranin counterstain was used</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="coupling-azo-dye-method-for-acid-phosphatase">Coupling azo-dye Method for Acid Phosphatase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coupling-azo-dye-method-for-acid-phosphatase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The enzyme hydrolyses the substrate, alpha naphthyl phosphate, to liberate alpha naphthol which couples with a diazonium salt to form an insoluble coloured azo-dye. This marks the site of enzyme activity. Fresh or fixed cryostat sections cut at 10–15 μm can be used.</p>
<p>Solution Dissolve 10–20 mg of sodium alpha naphthyl phosphate in 20 ml of 0.1 M hydrochloric acid- veronal buffer mixture at pH 5.0. Add 1.5 g polyvinyl pyrrolidone and leave to dissolve. Add approximately 20 mg of Fast Garnet GBC salt or Fast Red ITR.</p>
<p>Prepare veronal acetate solution:
Sodium acetate crystals 19.4 g
Sodium diethyl barbiturate (veronal) 29.4 g
Distilled water 1000 ml</p>
<p>To prepare buffer at pH 5.0, mix 25 ml of the veronal acetate solution, 36 ml of 0.1N HCl and 44 ml of distilled water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Filter the incubating medium onto the sections at 37 °C for 30–60 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in running water for 2 minutes.</li>
<li>Counterstain, if desired, in Mayer’s haemalum for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash thoroughly in running water for 30 minutes.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites of acid phosphatase activity : reddish brown
Nuclei : blue</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong>: Alternatively, 0.1 M acetate buffer may be used in place of veronal buffer.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d89fdc52">♦ ESTERASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d89fdc52" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The enzymes known as esterases hydrolyse esters of carboxylic acid. Generally they are sub-classified into aliesterases and azolesterases. The aliesterases include the non-specific esterases which will hydrolyse esters of long and short chain fatty acids. Azolesterases are the cholinesterase and acetylcholinesterase and these hydrolyse esters of choline and acetylcholine fatty acids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thiocholine-method-for-cholinesterase">Thiocholine Method for Cholinesterase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thiocholine-method-for-cholinesterase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cholinesterases will hydrolyse acetylcholine and the liberated thiocholine is precipitated as its</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>506 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<p>cupric salt. Fresh or fixed cryostat sections or teased preparations can be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Stock solution</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Copper sulphate 0.3 g</li>
<li>Glycine 0.375 g</li>
<li>Magnesium chloride 1.0 g</li>
<li>Maleic acid 1.75 g</li>
<li>1N (4%) sodium hydroxide 30 ml</li>
<li>Hot saturated (about 40%) sodium sulphate 170 ml</li>
<li>This solution keeps very well.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Working solution</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Distilled water 0.5 ml</li>
<li>Acetylthiocholine iodide 20 mg</li>
<li>Mix to dissolve.</li>
<li>Stock solution 10 ml</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Dilute solution of yellow ammonium sulphide.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Incubate sections in the incubating medium (working solution) at 37 °C for 20–40 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in three changes of saturated aqueous sodium sulphate.</li>
<li>Place in dilute ammonium sulphide for two minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites of enzyme activity: dark brown (cupric sulphide)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indoxyl-method-for-esterases">Indoxyl Method for Esterases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indoxyl-method-for-esterases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The substrate is indoxyl acetate, the esterases hydrolyse the substrate to release indoxyl. Additional oxidisers facilitate the transformation of the diffusable product of enzyme activity to insoluble indigo blue dye which marks the site of enzyme activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>2 M sodium chloride.</li>
<li>Barbital (veronal) hydrochloric acid buffer, pH 7.6</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>To test tube 1, add 1.51 mg of substrate.</li>
<li>To test tube 2, add in the following order:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>2 M sodium chloride 5 ml</li>
<li>Distilled deionised water 2 ml</li>
<li>Veronal-HCl buffer pH 7.6 2 ml</li>
<li>Potassium ferrocyanide solution 0.5 ml</li>
<li>Potassium ferricyanide solution 0.5 ml</li>
<li>Mix well.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Dissolve the substrate in five drops of absolute alcohol.</li>
<li>Add the solution in tube 2 to the substrate solution, mix well.</li>
<li>Add the mixture to the sections.</li>
<li>Incubate sections at 37 °C for 30–60 minutes.</li>
<li>When incubation is completed, rinse well in distilled water.</li>
<li>Counterstain, if desired, in 0.5% safranin O for 30 seconds</li>
<li>Rinse well in distilled water.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites of enzyme activity: indigo blue
Nuclei: red, if safranin counterstain was used</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Alternatively, 5-bromo-4’-chloroindoxyl acetate may be used as substrate.</li>
<li>Potassium ferrocyanide and ferricyanide are additional oxidisers.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="peptidases">PEPTIDASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peptidases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These enzymes which are also referred to as aminopeptidases hydrolyse peptide bonds. They release β-naphthylamine from the substrate and</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Enzyme Histochemistry 507</p>
<p>this reaction product couples with a diazo-compound to form an insoluble coloured final reaction product. Aminopeptidases are present in abundance in the kidney and the small intestine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="demonstration-of-leucine-aminopeptidase-lap">Demonstration of Leucine Aminopeptidase (LAP)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demonstration-of-leucine-aminopeptidase-lap" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The incubating medium consists of the substrate L-leucyl-β-naphthylamide and a diazonium salt. Fast Blue B. The enzyme liberates β-naphthylamine which couples with the diazonium salt to form a coloured insoluble complex which marks the site of enzyme activity. If the sections are treated with copper ions after incubation, the cupric ions chelate with the azo-dye that has been formed. This copper chelation also produces a positive charge on the azo-dye. Fresh frozen sections are used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-stock-substrate-solution">1. Stock substrate solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-stock-substrate-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Dissolve 8 mg per ml of L-leucyl β-naphthylamide in distilled water. Store in the refrigerator.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-incubating-medium">2. Incubating medium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-incubating-medium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Stock substrate solution</th><th>1 ml</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>0.1 M acetate buffer pH 6.5</td><td>10 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Sodium chloride (0.9%)</td><td>8 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Potassium cyanide (0.02 M)</td><td>1 ml</td></tr><tr><td>Fast blue B</td><td>10 mg</td></tr><tr><td>Adjust pH to 6.5 to 6.8.</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Cover section with incubating medium.</li>
<li>Incubate at 37°C for 20 minutes to two hours.</li>
<li>Rinse in 0.85% saline for 2–3 minutes.</li>
<li>Cover section with 0.1 M cupric sulphate for 2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in saline solution.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly or dehydrate, through graded alcohols, clear in xylene and mount in a synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites of leucine aminopeptidase activity : purplish blue.</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong></p>
<p>Potassium cyanide in the incubating medium acts as an activator.</p>
<p>It is extremely poisonous, and must be handled with care.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ccc74c1c">♦ OXIDATIVE ENZYMES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ccc74c1c" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The oxidative enzymes include the dehydrogenases, diaphorases, oxidases and peroxidases. They are all involved in catalysing reactions of the Krebs cycle and other similar pathways.</p>
<p>A large number of enzymes belong to the group of dehydrogenases, and they catalyse the transfer of hydrogen atoms from their specific substrate to hydrogen acceptors. They can either be aerobic dehydrogenases which transfer the hydrogen to molecular oxygen to produce hydrogen peroxide, or anaerobic dehydrogenases whose function is to transfer hydrogen to acceptors other than molecular oxygen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-for-succinate-dehydrogenase">Method for Succinate Dehydrogenase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-for-succinate-dehydrogenase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an anaerobic dehydrogenase which catalyses the reversible oxidation of succinic acid to fumaric acid. In the presence of a tetrazolium salt, the transfer of hydrogen reduces the tetrazolium salt to water-insoluble coloured formazan which marks the site of enzyme activity. Fresh frozen unfixed tissue should be used for cryostat sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>0.2 M phosphate buffer, pH 7.6</li>
</ol>
<p>0.2 M monobasic sodium phosphate (27.8 g/litre) 13 ml</p>
<p>0.2 M dibasic sodium phosphate (53.65 g/litre) 87 ml</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>0.2 M Sod. succinate</li>
</ol>
<p>(NaCOOCH₂–CH₂COONa, 6H₂O): (5.4 g/dl)</p>
<p>Mix fresh when needed.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Nitro blue tetrazolium (nitro BT or NBT) solution: 1 mg/ml</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>0.85% saline.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>508 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Formalin-saline (0.85 g of sodium chloride per 100 ml of 10% formalin).</li>
<li>15% ethanol.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Prepare incubation medium as follows:-
0.2 M phosphate buffer 5 ml
0.2 M Sod. succinate 5 ml
NBT solution 10 ml</li>
<li>Incubate sections in the above medium at 37 °C for 30 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash sections in saline.</li>
<li>Postfix in formalin-saline solution for 10 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse sections in 15% ethanol for 5 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in distilled water.</li>
<li>Counterstain, if desired, with 0.5% safranin O for 1/2 minute.</li>
<li>Rinse well in distilled water.</li>
<li>Mount in glycerine jelly, or dehydrate in alcohol, clear in xylene and mount in a synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong> Sites of enzyme activity: blue purple deposits of formazan pigment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="demonstration-of-nadph-diaphorase">Demonstration of NADPH Diaphorase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demonstration-of-nadph-diaphorase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Flavoprotein enzymes that are capable of transferring hydrogen from reduced nicotinamide adenine dinucleotide (NADH) and reduced nicotinamide adenine dinucleotide phosphate (NADPH) to various dyes are referred to as diaphorases. Tetrazolium salt is a ready hydrogen acceptor and the product of reduction is the water-insoluble formazan pigment. The enzymes are present in the kidney and skeletal muscle. Fresh frozen sections are used for the demonstration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>TRIS - hydrochloric acid buffer, pH 7.4
Tris (hydroxymethyl) aminomethane 6.5 g
Concentrated hydrochloric acid 3.34 ml
Distilled water 1000 ml</li>
<li>Nitro blue tetrazolium</li>
<li>NADPH</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Prepare the incubation medium as follows:
TRIS - hydrochloric acid buffer 10 ml
Nitro blue tetrazolium 10 mg
NADPH 4 mg
Adjust pH to 7.4</li>
<li>Incubate sections in this medium at 37 °C for 20–30 minutes.</li>
<li>Wash sections in distilled water for one minute.</li>
<li>Counterstain, if desired, with 0.5% soframin O for 1/2 minute.</li>
<li>Rinse well in distilled water.</li>
<li>Mount in aqueous mountant or dehydrate, clear and mount in a synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Site of enzyme activity: purplish</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="demonstration-of-the-oxidases">Demonstration of the Oxidases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demonstration-of-the-oxidases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This group of enzymes includes among others the cytochrome oxidase, tyrosinase (DOPA-Oxidase).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-for-cytochrome-oxidase">Method for Cytochrome Oxidase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-for-cytochrome-oxidase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is based on the so called ‘nadi’ reaction. Cytochrome oxidase catalyses the oxidative reaction between alpha-naphthol and dimethyl-para-phenylenediamine to form indophenol blue. Use unfixed fresh cryostat sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>0.1% solution of alpha naphthol in 1% sodium chloride and M/15 phosphate buffer (9.465 g Na₂HPO₄ dissolved in distilled water and made up to 1 litre) at pH 5.8.</li>
<li>0.1% solution of dimethyl-para phenylenediamine hydrochloride in 1% sodium chloride and M/15 phosphate buffer at pH 5.8.</li>
<li>‘Nadi’ reagent: Mix equal parts of the above solutions immediately before use.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Incubate the sections in the freshly prepared ‘Nadi’ reagent at 37 °C for at least five minutes and maximum one hour.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Enzyme Histochemistry 509</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Wash in 0.9% sodium chloride in distilled water.</li>
<li>If desired, counterstain nuclei in carmalum or any other red nuclear stain.</li>
<li>Mount in 5% potassium acetate in water.</li>
<li>Ring the coverslip with paraffin wax.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Sites of cytochrome enzyme
activity : bluish violet
Nuclei : red</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong> These preparations are not permanent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="demonstration-of-dopa-oxidase-tyrosinase">Demonstration of DOPA-oxidase (Tyrosinase)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demonstration-of-dopa-oxidase-tyrosinase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The enzyme, tyrosinase, is demonstrated by the action of Di-hydroxyphenylalanine (DOPA), which converts tyrosine into DOPA which is eventually converted to melanin.</p>
<p>Fresh or formalin fixed cryostat sections are used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Fix thin slices of tissue (1–2 mm) in 10% formalin for 1 hour at room temperature.</li>
<li>Wash in running water for three minutes.</li>
<li>Place in 0.1% DOPA in 0.1 M phosphate buffer at pH 7.4.</li>
<li>Incubate at 37 °C for one hour.</li>
<li>Transfer to fresh DOPA solution and leave at 37 °C for 10–12 hours.</li>
<li>Wash in running water.</li>
<li>Fix in Bouin’s fluid for 24 hours.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in alcohol, clear in toluene and embed in paraffin.</li>
<li>Cut sections 5μm and mount on slides.</li>
<li>Bring section to water, stain slightly with haematoxylin.</li>
<li>Dehydrate, clear and mount in a synthetic resin.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>DOPA-oxidase (tyrosinase) site : dark brown granules</p>
<p>Nuclei : blue</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="benzidine-method-for-peroxidase">Benzidine Method for Peroxidase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benzidine-method-for-peroxidase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Peroxidases catalyse the removal of oxygen from hydrogen peroxide to a suitable acceptor and release free oxygen. Benzidine, a colourless compound in the staining solution, is oxidised to blue dye by the free oxygen. Benzidine is carcinogenic and should be handled with care. Fresh unfixed cryostat sections are used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>1% ammonium molybdate solution in 0.9% sodium chloride.</li>
<li>Saturated solution of benzidine in 0.9% sodium chloride.</li>
<li>Picric acid in 95% alcohol.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Place sections in the 1% ammonium molybdate solution in 0.9% sodium chloride for four–five minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer sections to a saturated solution of benzidine containing a few drops of 20 volume hydrogen peroxide and leave for about three minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer to a saturated solution of picric acid in 95% alcohol, leave for five minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in tap water, dehydrate, clear and mount in a synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Peroxidase granules : dark blue
Cytoplasm : yellow</p>
<p><strong>Notes</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>In step 2, about 1 ml H₂O₂ to 25 ml benzidine solution is adequate.</li>
<li>The peroxidase present in the thyroid epithelium is also demonstrated.</li>
<li>This peroxidase is labile while the leucocyte enzyme is stable. It can be eliminated by treating the section first with 10% formalin for about 10–15 minutes. The leucocyte peroxidase is unaffected.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251218-2891293c.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electron-microscopy-in-histopathology">Electron Microscopy in Histopathology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electron-microscopy-in-histopathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are several techniques and methods required and employed for transmission electron microscopy (TEM) by the electron microscope (EM) histotechnologist. It is not possible to cover all the methods of electron microscopy in a book of this nature. Attempt is made here to give general information with regard to methods, equipment and reagents of each step of normal processing or specimens from surgical pathology tissues. The reader is therefore referred to a standard book of histopathology for additional detailed in-depth study and information on this topic.</p>
<p>Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) is not a fast diagnostic procedure since it takes several days for results as opposed to frozen sections which takes an hour or less, or general routine histology that produces results within 24–48 hours. It nevertheless offers information and answers to questions in long term diseases involving the kidneys, lungs and tumours among others. In most cases, such information complements light microscopy, histochemistry and histoimmunology.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fixation">FIXATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most important step in preparing material for electron microscopy is the fixation. It is very essential to fix surgical tissue within 15 minutes of it being removed from the patient’s body. This is to prevent cellular changes due to autolysis and to obtain a correct picture of the cells in the tissue. The properties of fixatives for electron microscopy are similar to those for light microscopy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="commonly-used-fixatives">Commonly Used Fixatives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#commonly-used-fixatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Every fixative has some special properties which make it more preferable than another. One common feature is that tissues taken for fixation should be minced in about 1 ml volume of fixative in order to ensure proper infiltration and fixation of all portions of the tissue especially with the slow penetrating fixatives. The most widely used fixatives are:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Zamboni’s fixative</strong> This is a mixture of picric acid and paraformaldehyde that is buffered with phosphate. It penetrates fairly rapidly, preserves optimally and is stable at room temperature for up to one year. This fixative allows post-osmication, and allows the fixed material to be kept at room temperature.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Paraformaldehyde-glutaraldehyde</strong> This mixture is also sometimes called formaldehyde glutaldehyde (F-G) because of the dissociation of paraformaldehyde to formaldehyde. It penetrates rapidly with little shrinkage. It is important to make it fresh because it tends to become too acidic and it should be kept in the refrigerator. Microtubules are well preserved but lipids are extracted.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Electron Microscopy in Histopathology 511</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Glutaraldehyde, 2-3% This is a slow acting fixative. The big advantage in its favour is its excellent preservation of tissues. It must be prepared fresh and regularly checked for acidity as the pH decreases with time. Ideally stock solutions in 8% or 25% concentration are prepared and sealed in vials which are kept in the refrigerator until ready to use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Osmium tetroxide This is used as 1% in phosphate buffered saline (PBS), pH 7.4. It is stable for only few days in the refrigerator when diluted. It must be used with caution and in the fume cabinet because it is a very caustic substance.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dehydration">DEHYDRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dehydration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dehydration of tissues for EM is carried out starting with a lower grade of alcohol (40%). The concentrations and number of grades chosen depends upon the type of tissue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clearing">CLEARING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The clearing agents in EM are referred to as transitional fluids and consist of media miscible with ethanol and embedding medium. Examples are xylene, toluene and epoxypropane (propylene oxide).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="embedding">EMBEDDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#embedding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Thin sections (50–90 nm) are used in TEM in order for the electrons to penetrate and allow photons to reach the fluorescent viewing screen of the EM. For routine purposes, the epoxy resins are employed. These resins are relatively easy to handle and are fairly easily available. Paraffin is much too soft to permit ultra thin sections to be cut. The most commonly used types of epoxy resins are those with an Araldite base and those with an Epon 812 base. Araldite, a resin that is relatively stable under electron bombardments, is soluble in acetone and ethanol. Araldite formulas for embedding must be prepared with great care so as to obtain the correct consistency. Epon resin is also stable in the face of electron bombardment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sectioning-for-electron-microscope">SECTIONING FOR ELECTRON MICROSCOPE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sectioning-for-electron-microscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The electron microscope and its principle have been discussed under Microscopy in Section 1. Thick and thin sections are cut with an ultramicrotome (Fig. 5.7). The thick sections are cut at between 0.5 and 2 mm and they are used to study general picture of the tissue and to locate area of special interest, such as a glomerulus in a kidney biopsy. These sections are cut with glass knives.</p>
<p>Thin sections are usually cut at between 50 and 90 nm and appear grey in reflected light colours. These sections are cut with diamond knives if available, otherwise fresh or new glass knives may also be used. Some laboratories prefer to make their own glass knives instead of purchasing from knife making companies. They claim it is cheaper to do that. However, both the glass and diamond knives are readily available commercially.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="materials-used-for-cutting-thick-and-thin-sections">Materials Used for Cutting Thick and Thin Sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#materials-used-for-cutting-thick-and-thin-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Microscope slides for thick sections Cleaned slides with frosted ends, with a ringed area in the centre made with wax pencil when slides are warmed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Applicator sticks with whittled tips These are used to clean knife edge after soaking them in distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hair brushes These are used for orienting thick and thin sections for pick up and removal of unwanted sections. It is best to use eyelashes or straight hair.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rose lens paper This lens paper is used for wiping debris from trough surfaces and drying grids.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>2 ml disposable syringe with needle This is for filling and adjusting floatation fluid level in the knife trough.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Floatation medium The medium is distilled water or acetone in a small container. The 2 ml syringe and needle is used to withdraw the medium to fill the knife trough.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staining-of-thick-sections">Staining of Thick Sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-of-thick-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A variety of stains has been used to stain thick sections in electron microscopy. The most effective of these stains are the basic dyes. Toluidine blue and Trypan blue in 1% sodium borate have proved very useful. The toluidine blue is metachromatic in reaction and accentuates cytoplasmic differentiation. Equally important is the fact that it is simple and easy to make up and also gives reproducible results. Trypan blue is used as 2% in 1% sodium borate. It is similar to toluidine blue in action and procedures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staining-of-thin-sections">Staining of Thin Sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-of-thin-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Uranyl and lead stains are the more widely employed stains for thin sections. An important factor common to both stains is the possession of electron dense metal which is essential for proper contrast in cellular components for photomicrography.</p>
<p>Uranyl acetate is a nuclear stain, and specifically binds to nuclear proteins. It is used in saturated concentration in distilled water. It has a tendency to break down or dissociate so that the stock solution should not be kept in the refrigerator beyond one month. It is also soluble in alcohol. Many workers prefer to use 25% to 50% concentration in ethyl or methyl alcohol. The alcoholic solution penetrates faster and requires a shorter staining time of about 2 to 5 minutes. The solubility of uranyl acetate is dependent on temperature and the solution should be kept tightly covered in the refrigerator.</p>
<p>Lead citrate is a cytoplasmic stain. It intensifies the detail of cellular membrane and inclusions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="materials-required-to-place-grids-in-electron-microscope-column">Materials Required to Place Grids in Electron Microscope Column<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#materials-required-to-place-grids-in-electron-microscope-column" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Lint-free cloths</li>
<li>Lint-free gloves</li>
<li>No. 5 straight or 7 curved electron microscope forceps</li>
<li>Hand lens to observe centering and quality of section (this is optional).</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Chapter 16
Cytology</p>
<p>Cytology is the study of free cells from different organs of the body. These cells may have been shed by the body itself; aspirated by tube or needle; or scraped or washed from tissue surfaces. Therefore, effusions, secretions, aspirates and scrapings are all used in diagnostic cytology. Exfoliative cytology is the study of cells which are shed spontaneously from epithelial surfaces of the body. This spontaneous shedding is a function of normal epithelium. The epithelial surfaces undergo constant growth and so they continue to shed worn out cells which are replaced by new ones. However, malignant tumour cells exfoliate more readily than those from healthy tissues. The detection of malignant cells in clinical specimens under microscopic examination is the most important role of diagnostic cytology. In addition, valuable information may be obtained about infections and infestations, reproductive defects and hormonal status. Clinical specimens are obtained with little or no discomfort to the patient.</p>
<p>All clinical specimens sent to the Cytology laboratory should be regarded as potentially pathogenic. Therefore, all safety precautions applicable to Microbiology laboratory should also be applied here. Safety cabinets are a must for processing sputum. Disinfectant jars should be placed at strategic points on the work bench and the staff should wear protective clothing.</p>
<p>Cytology has become a strong diagnostic tool for the early detection and diagnosis of malignancy in different organs of the body, in the assessment of hormonal activity which is valuable in some cases of infertility and in the evaluation of certain endocrine disorders.</p>
<p>In exfoliative cytology, the microscopic evaluation is based upon observation and characteristics of the basic cells. Since a majority of the cells are in the form of single cast off cells lying in a fluid medium, there is no distortion to their shapes. This is unlike histopathology where the arrangement of cell aggregates is the basis of diagnosis of malignancy. Most of the information from the study of discrete cells is based on the shape or size of the nuclei. Cytoplasm of the cells may only assist in identifying the cell type. Figure 16.1 shows some of the characteristic nuclear abnormalities associated with carcinomas. They are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Nuclear enlargement with no increase in the overall cell size, showing a decreased cytoplasm/nucleus ratio.</li>
<li>Irregularity of nuclear outline with variation in size and shape.</li>
<li>Hyperchromasia. This is as a result of increased amounts of deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA); the nuclei of malignant cells often stain more intensely with basic dyes.</li>
<li>Multinucleation due to abnormal cell division.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>514 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251218-64fe9982.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg">
Fig. 16.1 Diagrammatic presentation of cellular abnormalities in carcinoma</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Uneven distribution and variation in size of chromatin particles.</li>
<li>Increase in size and number of nucleoli.</li>
</ol>
<p>To achieve a meaningful result and interpretation, smears should be prepared from fresh specimens and fixed while still wet. The nature of the specimen, the age of cell population, method of collection and fixation will all affect morphology of the cells. Most importantly, a prompt and proper fixation is essential.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fixation">FIXATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A good cytological fixative should penetrate rapidly with no distortion to the cell morphology.</p>
<p>The clinician, in most cases, prepares and fixes the smear in the clinic or at bed side. The laboratory should make available to the wards and outpatients' clinic, a container and carrier for smear fixatives in the form of a polythene screw-capped coplin jar grooved to take up to 8–10 slides.</p>
<p>If the smears are to be sent by post to a distant laboratory, aerosol fixative sprays give an effective form of fixation. These aerosol sprays consist usually of an alcohol and wax—the alcohol fixes the smear and the wax sets to provide a water-soluble protective film. Some laboratories coat pre-fixed smears with glycerine or water soluble wax. Alternatively, the smears may be air-dried after complete fixation and then placed in suitable cardboard, plastic or wooden slide box-carrier designed and grooved to hold a few slides.</p>
<p>Fluids of larger volumes, e.g., pleural or peritoneal effusion, or sputum, should be sent to the laboratory immediately after collection and smears can then be made.</p>
<p>The most widely used fixatives are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Alcohol-ether (equal parts of diethyl ether and 95% alcohol) mixture.</li>
<li>95% alcohol with or without 3% glacial acetic acid.</li>
<li>A mixture of seven parts of tertiary butyl alcohol and three parts of 95% alcohol.</li>
<li>Schaudinn’s solution:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Saturated aqueous mercuric chloride 66 ml</li>
<li>Absolute ethyl alcohol 33 ml</li>
<li>Glacial acetic acid 0.3 ml</li>
</ul>
<p>Fixation time in any of these fixatives is at least 15 minutes and maximum 7 days.</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Cytology 515</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subdivisions-of-cytology">SUBDIVISIONS OF CYTOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subdivisions-of-cytology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For practical purposes, cytology is subdivided as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Gynaecological Cytology (Gynae-cytology) This deals with the cytology of the vagina, cervix and endometrium.</li>
<li>Non-gynaecological cytology This is the cytology of cells suspended in body fluids.</li>
<li>Fine needle aspiration cytology (FNAC) The study of cells aspirated from organs and structures of the body.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gynaecological-cytology">GYNAECOLOGICAL CYTOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gynaecological-cytology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are three most important applications of gynae-cytology:</p>
<p>(i) The detection of malignancy—mainly cancer of cervix.
(ii) Assessment of hormonal activity
(iii) Identification of vaginal infection and inflammatory conditions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specimen-collection-and-preparation-of-smears">Specimen Collection and Preparation of Smears<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specimen-collection-and-preparation-of-smears" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Cervical smears Cervical smears are made from material collected with the help of a speculum (a metal or plastic device) which is inserted into the vagina and allows the uterine cervix to be readily visible. A specialised spatula known as the Ayre spatula or cervical spatula (Fig. 16.2.) is used for collection. The collection is made at the junction of the columnar epithelium by visualising the cervix, the spatula is inserted via the speculum into the cervical os and rotated through 360 degrees. The material collected is quickly smeared over a pre-labelled microscope slide and fixed immediately.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251218-daf9b957.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg">
Fig. 16.2 Ayre spatula</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Aspiration from the posterior fornix With the aid of a speculum, cellular material is collected from the posterior fornix, using a disposable plastic pipette with a suction bulb (Fig. 16.3). Following aspiration, smears are prepared and fixed immediately.</li>
<li>Vaginal smears Vaginal smears are valuable for the assessment of hormonal function. Cellular material is collected by scraping the upper third of the lateral wall of the vagina with a wooden spatula. The cells are evenly and thinly smeared over a clean pre-labelled microscope slide and fixed.</li>
<li>Endocervical smears This is used mainly for follow up cases where a surgical treatment has been used after a cone biopsy has been taken for assessment of dysplasia and malignancy or as a curative procedure. A cotton tip swab is inserted into the endocervix and rotated gently to cover a wide area of the endocervix. The material collected is smeared on a clean pre-labelled microscope slide and fixed.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251218-6448d75f.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg">
Fig. 16.3 Disposable plastic pipetter with a suction pump for aspiration of posterior fornix</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>516 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Endometrial aspiration This procedure has to be performed under strict aseptic conditions so as not to introduce infection into the patient. A cannula is inserted into the uterine cavity and the cellular material is aspirated using a syringe. Thin smears are made on clean pre-labelled slides and fixed.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining">STAINING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most commonly used stain in the gynae-cytology is the Papanicoloau stain. It is a stain specially suitable for cervical smears. It gives sharp nuclear staining and good differential colouring of acidophilic and basophilic cells. It makes the cytoplasm transparent. There are other stains that can be effectively used for diagnostic purposes in the gynae-cytology.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="papanicoloau-staining-method">Papanicoloau Staining Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#papanicoloau-staining-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This staining method can be performed either manually when there are only a few slides to deal with, or by using automatic staining machine when a large number of slides is to be stained.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Harris haematoxylin (see Chapter 7)</li>
<li>Orange G solution (OG 6)
0.5% Orange G (C1 No.16230) in 95% alcohol 100 ml
Phosphotungstic acid 0.015 g</li>
<li>Eosin Azure 50 (E.A. 50 or E A 36):
0.5% light green SF (Yellowish) (C1 No. 42095) in 95% alcohol 45 ml
0.5% Bismark brown Y (C1 No.21000) in 95% alcohol 10 ml
0.5% Eosin (C1 No.45380) in 95% alcohol 45 ml
Phosphotungstic acid 0.2 g
Saturated aqueous lithium carbonate 1 drop
Mix well and store in tightly capped, brown bottles.</li>
</ol>
