<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure-for-manual-staining">Procedure for manual staining<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-for-manual-staining" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Remove smears from fixative.</li>
<li>Rinse in descending grades of alcohol (80, 70 and 50%) and water for 10 seconds each.</li>
<li>Stain in Harris haematoxylin for 2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in water for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Differentiate in 1% acid alcohol until only the nuclei retain the stain (a few seconds).</li>
<li>Wash and blue in tap water for 3–5 minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer to 70% alcohol for a few seconds.</li>
<li>Transfer to 95% alcohol for a few seconds.</li>
<li>Stain in OG 6 for 2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in 2 changes of 95% alcohol.</li>
<li>Stain in EA 50 for 2–4 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in 2 changes of 95% alcohol.</li>
<li>Dehydrate in absolute alcohol, clear in xylene and mount in neutral synthetic medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nuclei :Blue
Acidophilic (superficial) cells :reddish-pink
Basophilic (intermediate and parabasal cells) <span style="color: rgb(0, 104, 201);"></span>/green
Candida albicans :Red to pale pink
Trichomonas vaginalis <span style="color: rgb(85, 88, 103);"></span> green</p>
<p><strong>Note</strong> EA 50 or EA 36 and OG 6 are available commercially.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure-for-automatic-staining">Procedure for automatic staining<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-for-automatic-staining" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fixed smears to:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Trough</th><th>Solutions</th><th>Time in minutes</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td>70% alcohol</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>50% alcohol</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Distilled water</td><td>2</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Harris haematoxylin</td><td>3</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Distilled water</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>Tap water</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>0.5% HCl in 70% ethanol</td><td>1/2</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>Tap water</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>Tap water</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>70% alcohol</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>70% alcohol</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>95% alcohol</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>95% alcohol</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td>OG 6</td><td>2</td></tr></tbody></table>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormone-assessment">HORMONE ASSESSMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormone-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As part of a general investigation into the cause of human reproductive disorder and sterility among women, hormone assessment is done.</p>
<p>Hormonal activity can be evaluated on the basis of microscopic examination of Papanicoloau stained vaginal smears. The karyopyknotic index (KPI) and the maturation index (MI) are the two methods commonly used to assess hormone activity.</p>
<p>Superficial cornified squamous epithelial cells show condensed, deeply stained, structureless (pyknotic) nuclei, with pink to red stained cytoplasm. The calculation of KPI is done by counting a total of 200 squamous cells in a Papanicoloau stained smear. The cornified squamous cells are expressed as a percentage of the total number of squamous cells. In order to obtain a meaningful assessment of the hormonal (oestrogenic) influence, smears are taken at about 3 or 4 days interval throughout the menstrual cycle.</p>
<p>The maturation index (MI) is based on cell maturation which is determined by means of the morphology and staining reactions of the non-cornified squamous epithelial cells. These are classified as superficial intermediate and parabasal cells. A total of at least 200 squamous cells are counted and each class of cells is expressed as a percentage. High oestrogenic activity is indicated by a preponderance of superficial intermediate cells while low activity is indicated by a predominance of parabasal cells. Another good staining method used for the assessment of hormonal function is the Shorr's method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="shorr-s-staining-method">Shorr's Staining Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shorr-s-staining-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method uses a single differential staining solution. It gives less cytoplasmic transparency and poorer nuclear definition than the Papanicoloau. It is not very useful in the diagnosis of malignant cells.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="staining-solution">Staining solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>50% ethyl alcohol</th><th>100 ml</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Biebrich scarlet (CI No.26905)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>water-soluble</td><td>0.5 g</td></tr><tr><td>Orange G (CI No.16230)</td><td>0.25 g</td></tr><tr><td>Fast green FCF (CI No.42053)</td><td>0.075 g</td></tr><tr><td>Phosphotungstic acid</td><td>0.5 g</td></tr><tr><td>Phosphomolybdic acid</td><td>0.5 g</td></tr><tr><td>Glacial acetic acid</td><td>1 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Fix smear in alcohol-ether for 1–2 minutes</li>
<li>Stain in Shorr stain for 1–2 minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse in 70% alcohol to remove excess stain.</li>
<li>Transfer to 95% alcohol for 3 seconds.</li>
<li>Transfer to absolute alcohol for 3 seconds.</li>
<li>Clear in xylene and mount in a neutral synthetic resin.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Nuclei : Red
Superficial cornified cells : Bright orange-red
Non-cornified cells : Green-blue</p>
<p>There are other stains which, though less effective, can be used in gynae-cytology. Some of these are:</p>
<p>(i) Haematoxylin and Eosin
(ii) Acridine orange fluorescence technique
(iii) Feulgen’s reaction for DNA for research work.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sex-chromatin-barr-bodies">Sex Chromatin (Barr bodies)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sex-chromatin-barr-bodies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sex chromatin is present in about 30% of cells from the female whereas cells from the male do not have the sex chromatin. The sex chromatin appears as a darkly staining dot in the nucleus. It is present</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>518 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<p>in the cells of the skin, cells of the buccal mucosa and in the cells of blood, notably the leucocytes. Specimens are conveniently obtained by scrapings of the buccal mucosa.</p>
<p>The Barr bodies are normally seen attached to the nuclear membrane of the epithelial cells. It is sometimes used to determine the sex of an individual.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cresyl-fast-violet-acetate-method-for-demonstrating-sex-chromatin">Cresyl Fast Violet Acetate Method for Demonstrating Sex Chromatin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cresyl-fast-violet-acetate-method-for-demonstrating-sex-chromatin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a rapid, simple and effective method for demonstrating sex chromatin. It requires no differentiation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="staining-solution">Staining solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Cresyl fast violet acetate 1.0 g
Distilled water 100 ml</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Fix smear while still wet in 95% alcohol for three minutes.</li>
<li>Transfer to 50% alcohol for a few seconds and then to distilled water.</li>
<li>Stain with cresyl fast violet acetate solution for five minutes.</li>
<li>Rinse quickly in tap water.</li>
<li>Dehydrate with 95% alcohol, then with absolute alcohol.</li>
<li>Clear in two changes of xylene and mount in a neutral synthetic resin medium.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="results">Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Sex chromatin :deeply stained
Cytoplasm :faintly stained.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong> This method is treated under Gynae-cytology for convenience. Specimens of bronchial washings or lavage should be centrifuged and smears made and fixed immediately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="82046ebf">♦ NON-GYNAECOLOGICAL CYTOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#82046ebf" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This aspect of cytology involves the study of cells suspended in body fluids. The specimens are varied and are taken from various parts of the body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sputum">Sputum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sputum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sputum specimen is valuable for the study of respiratory tract disorders. It is used in the diagnosis of the following abnormal conditions.</p>
<p>(i) Malignant disease of the lower respiratory tract.
(ii) Pulmonary asbestosis
(iii) Pulmonary inflammatory conditions due to fungal infection, bacterial infection, viral infection or parasitic infection.</p>
<p>Sputum is normally collected as early morning deep cough specimens, and is preferably submitted on three consecutive days. It is not advisable to collect sputum specimen after a recent bronchoscopy has been done. The result will be invalidated by the presence of numerous inflammatory cells which could obscure some underlying pathology. As much as possible, sputum should be sent to the laboratory promptly and smears made as soon as possible. However, sputum specimens are well preserved when refrigerated at 4 °C.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="preparation-of-smears">Preparation of smears<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-smears" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Sputum must be processed in a biological safety cabinet. Purulent or blood stained particles are selected from the sputum with a microbiological wire loop and used to make thin smears, at least two smears from each specimen.</p>
<p>Bronchial washings are usually submitted in sterile containers. They are centrifuged without delay and smears made from the sediment. They can also be spun at 150 rpm for 10 minutes in a cytocentrifuge directly onto a clean pre-labelled microscope slides and fixed immediately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fixation">Fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Fixation should be carried out while the smears are still wet. Many workers prefer to use 3% acetic acid in 95% alcohol.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pleural-fluid-and-ascitic-fluid">Pleural Fluid and Ascitic Fluid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pleural-fluid-and-ascitic-fluid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are serous fluids that normally lubricate the walls of pleural and peritoneal cavities. They increase in volume and contain cells under certain pathological conditions. Cytological examination</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Cytology 519</p>
<p>of these fluids may reveal malignant cells which may arise from tumours of the surrounding mesothelium or they may be metastatic deposits.</p>
<p><strong>Collection and preparation of smears</strong> By means of a needle or canula with an attached syringe, the specimens are aspirated from the pleural or peritoneal cavities. The aspirated material is transferred into a sterile container and sent to the laboratory. The specimens are centrifuged at 300 rpm for 10 minutes or cytospun at 1500 rpm for 10 minutes, and thin smears made, at least two smears from each specimen. Any clots that are formed are fixed and processed histologically.</p>
<p><strong>Fixation</strong> Fixation, as usual, should be carried out promptly and while still wet. However, if the choice of stain is Romanowsky, then the smear should be air dried and then fixed with methanol before commencing the staining procedure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gastric-brushing-or-lavage">Gastric Brushing or Lavage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gastric-brushing-or-lavage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These types of specimens are very useful in the diagnosis of squamous cell carcinoma of the oesophagus or adenocarcinoma of the stomach. The collection of specimen is by the insertion of a small brush into the oesophagus or into the stomach under endoscopic guidance or by x-ray guidance. The brush is rotated at the particular spot of interest; the material is then smeared on a clean pre-labelled microscope slide and fixed immediately. If specimen of washing or lavage is obtained, then this is treated as the pleural or peritoneal fluids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="urine">Urine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Urine cytology is of great value in the diagnosis of urethral tumours, urinary bladder carcinoma, carcinoma of the kidney and carcinoma of the prostate in males. Normal urine contains few or no cells; but under certain pathological conditions, the urine contains many abnormal cells. Early morning specimens of urine are preferred because they give larger concentration of cells due to relatively long residence in the bladder.</p>
<p><strong>Fixation</strong> Urine tends to wash off slides during fixation and staining due to the low protein content. This difficulty may be overcome by</p>
<p>(i) Centrifuging the sample and making smears with the sediment on albuminised slides;
(ii) The urine sediment is mixed with some drops of egg albumin and then smeared or
(iii) Celloidinising of the slides after fixation.</p>
<p>An initial fixation or preservation can be done on urine sample that may not get to the laboratory in good time. This is by adding 50% alcohol to the specimen in equal proportion.</p>
<p><strong>Staining</strong> For non-Gynae-cytology, the Papanicoloau stain is equally as useful as in the Gynae-cytology but many workers prefer to use it as a confirmatory procedure. The common staining methods are:</p>
<p><strong>The Romanowsky staining methods</strong> Following fixation in ether-alcohol, smears may be stained by any of the Romanowsky’s stains. Alternatively, a fluid specimen may be smeared and air dried and then fixed with methanol for five minutes before applying the Romanowsky stain. For technique of Romanowsky staining, please refer to the Haematology Section.</p>
<p>The staining is satisfactory for cells in fluids and effusions. The most popular Romanowsky stains are the Giemsa and the Leishman stains.</p>
<p><strong>Methylene blue</strong> This single-stain, rapid and simple method is useful for the screening of fresh specimens, especially sputum, for malignant cells. The preparation is not permanent and should be examined immediately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staining-solution">Staining solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staining-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Methylene blue</th><th>1 g</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Distilled water</td><td>100 ml</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Place a small amount of fresh purulent sputum, or two drops of centrifuged deposit of the body fluid on a clean microscope slide.</li>
<li>Add one drop of the stain to the specimen on the slide and mix the two together thoroughly.</li>
</ol>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>520 Histopathological Techniques and Cytology</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Cover the mixture with a clean cover slip and spread by gentle pressure</li>
<li>Examine immediately.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>Nuclei : shades of blue.</p>
<p>Any suspicious cell is confirmed using other more specific staining techniques.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acridine-orange-fluorescence-method">Acridine Orange Fluorescence Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acridine-orange-fluorescence-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is based on the principle that the fluorochrome dye, acridine orange, which has an affinity for nucleic acids, can emit visible light when excited by an ultra violet or blue light, usually of 350–400 nm Wavelength. At pH 6.0, this dye will demonstrate DNA green or greenish-yellow and RNA orange-red with fluorescence microscopy. Malignant cells have a large amount of RNA in their cytoplasm and so they are readily seen by their orange or red fluorescence under low power magnification. This method permits quick scanning of smear preparation. Positive or doubtful cases are usually confirmed by Papanicoloau stain.</p>
<p><strong>Solutions</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>0.067M Potassium dihydrogen orthophosphate:
Dissolve 9.072g of potassium dihydrogen phosphate (KH₂PO₄) in 1000 ml distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>0.067 M Disodium hydrogen orthophosphate:
Dissolve 9.465g of disodium hydrogen ortho-phosphate, anhydrous (Na₂HPO₄) in 1000 ml distilled water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Phosphate buffer (pH 6.0):
87.8 ml of solution 1 are mixed with 12.2 ml of solution 2</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acridine orange stock solution:
Acridine orange (CI No.46005) 0.1 g
Distilled water 100 ml
Store in a dark bottle at 4 °C.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acridine orange staining solution:
Acridine orange stock solution 10 ml
Phosphate buffer (pH 6.0) 90 ml</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>0.1 M Calcium chloride differentiator:
Calcium chloride (CaCl₂) 11.099 g</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="distilled-water">Distilled water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#distilled-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Procedure</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Fix smear in ether-alcohol mixture for 15 minutes.</li>
<li>Pass through descending grades of alcohol (80, 70 and 50%) to distilled water.</li>
<li>Rinse briefly in 1% acetic acid and wash in two changes of distilled water for one minute each.</li>
<li>Stain in acridine orange staining solution for three minutes.</li>
<li>Wash in phosphate buffer for one minute.</li>
<li>Differentiate with 0.1M calcium chloride until the nuclei are clearly outlined (about one minute).</li>
<li>Wash thoroughly with phosphate buffer solution.</li>
<li>Mount with a cover slip using phosphate buffer as the mountant.</li>
<li>Examine by fluorescence microscopy.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Results</strong></p>
<p>.NA fluorescence : red
DNA fluorescence : green</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Note</strong>
&gt; Certain normal cells and micro-organisms also show varying degrees of orange-red fluorescence. Therefore experience is required to be able to identify cells and cellular morphology.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="haematoxylin-and-eosin-method">Haematoxylin and Eosin Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haematoxylin-and-eosin-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Following fixation, it is possible to bring smears to water through descending grades of alcohol and then stain with haematoxylin and eosin as for sections. The H and E gives good result but lacks the transparency of cytoplasm that is seen in Papanicoloau technique.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cedf5f5">♦ FINE NEEDLE ASPIRATION CYTOLOGY (FNAC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cedf5f5" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before the advent of this procedure about two decades ago, the needle cone biopsy was the method</p>
<p>Scanned by CamScanner</p>
<p>Cytology 521</p>
<p>employed to collect material from lesions in the organs that do not normally exfoliate cells. The fine needle aspiration technique has almost completely superseded the more traumatic method of cone biopsy.</p>
<p>For aspiration of specimens, the FNAC basically requires a sterile syringe and needle, the length of the needle depending on the location of the organ to be sampled. The needle thickness is usually in the range of 0.5–0.9 mm. A special handle can be attached to the syringe to allow single hand grip, freeing the other hand for palpation and fixation of the mass if it is mobile (Fig. 16.4)</p>
<p>To perform the aspiration, first of all, the skin is cleaned with a suitable antiseptic. The mass is then immobilised with one hand. Without the piston of the syringe being retracted, the needle is inserted into the mass. The cells are then aspirated into the needle. The needle can be inserted from different angles if the material from one site is too scanty. Release the piston before withdrawing the needle. This is to equilibrate the pressure in order to prevent the material being drawn into the barrel of the syringe.</p>
<p>The collected specimen is expressed on to a clean pre-labelled slide (or slides) and spread evenly. Fixation is done immediately and stained with Papanicoloau or H and E stains. Any tissue fragments seen in the aspirate are fixed, processed and stained histologically. Lesions that cannot be localised by touch (non-palpable) are visualised by means of ultrasonography or fluoroscopy. The ultrasonography is for abdominal aspiration while fluoroscopy is used for bone and thoracic lesions.</p>
<p>FNAC is very valuable for preliminary diagnosis of carcinomas as well as inflammatory conditions. It is rapid and fairly inexpensive. But experience is required to correctly interpret staining result. FNAC is particularly useful in dealing with suspected masses or lesions on the skin, lymph node, breast, thyroid, liver, kidney, lung and bone.</p>

(d)</p>
<p>The technique of aspiration biopsy</p>
<p>(a) Needle is inserted into the mass.
(b) The piston is retracted to aspirate the sample.
(c) The needle is moved back and forth at different angles to aspirate more material.
(d) The piston is released before withdrawing the needle from the mass.</p>
<p>Fig. 16.4 Syringe and needle used for FNAC</p>
